Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Praying with an Impure Garment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on praying with an impure garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to APPLY the Hanafi rule for praying with an impure garment when unable to purify it, and IDENTIFY the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Two Disciples.

Core Idea
When unable to purify an impure garment, choose the lesser of two evils: pray standing in it or naked sitting—both valid.

This lesson tackles a practical dilemma: your only garment is impure and you cannot clean it. The Hanafi school allows a choice, while other views insist on praying in the garment. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your fiqh intuition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The situation: a person has a garment that is impure (najis). He cannot remove the impurity, nor can he find a pure garment, nor can he reduce the impurity (e.g., by washing part). The garment may be entirely impure or have a pure part less than a quarter.
If the pure part is more than a quarter, the garment is considered pure and prayer is valid normally.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa (walahu) says he has a choice: either pray standing in the impure garment with bowing and prostration, or pray naked sitting with gestures (imaa'). Standing in the impure garment is better.
This applies to both cases: pure part less than a quarter or entire garment impure.
3
State Zufar and Muhammad's position
Zufar and Muhammad (wa lahuma) say he must pray in the impure garment with bowing and prostration; praying naked is not allowed.
Their reasoning: the command to purify fell due to inability, but the command to cover remains because he has the garment, even if impure.
4
Analyze the evidence
Each side presents arguments. Abu Hanifa: the command is to cover with a pure garment; if pure is impossible, the command falls. Substitutes (gestures) fulfill postures. Choose the easier affliction. Zufar/Muhammad: praying in impure garment leaves one obligation unfulfilled, while praying naked leaves several.
The text provides an analogy: if standing causes wind to escape, he sits and gestures.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The text states 'he has a choice', indicating Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon. However, standing in the impure garment is still better.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعورة الغليظة: وهي الدبر والذكر والأنثيان، أي حكمها حكم الساق في أن انكشاف ربعه مانع. (ط) والأمة: [القنة أو المدبرة أو المكاتبة وغيرها. (ط)] لقول عمر الله : "ألقي عنك الخمار يا دفار (أي المنتنة) أتشبهين بالحرائر" لما رأى جارية متقنعة، فالحكمة في منعه من التشبه بالحرائر أن السفهاء جرت عادتهم بالتعرض للإماء، فخشي عمر رضي الله عنه أن يلتبس الأمر فتكون الفتنة أشد ، قال تعالى: ﴿ذَلِكَ أَدْنَى أَنْ يُعْرَفْنَ فَلَا يُؤْذَيْنَ ﴾ (الأحزاب: ٥٩) ولأنها تخرج لحاجة مولاها في ثياب الخدمة عادة فاعتبر حالها بذوات المحارم في حق الرجال دفعا للحرج. (فتح) كالرجل في أن عورتها من تحت سرتها إلى تحت ركبتها (ط) وظهرها وبطنها : لأن النظر إليهما سبب [# لا توجد إشارة #] لأنها محل الشهوة دونه وكل من الظهر والبطن موضع مشتهى. [البحر الرائق: ٥٣٧/١] عورة: أيضاً، والجنب تبع للبطن، والخنثى الرقيق كالأمة، والحرّ كالحرّة. ولو وجد ثوبا إلخ أي فإن كان الأكثر من الربع طاهراً أولى أن لا تجوز صلاته؛ لأن الربع يحكي حكاية الكل، وهذا إذا لم يجد ما يزيل به النجاسة ولا ما يقللها صلى معها و لم يعد ، ولا يجوز صلاته عرياناً. (فتح) لم تجز: صلاته لأن للربع حكم الكل كما في الإحرام. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٠/١] وخير بين أن يصلي عريانا قاعدا بإيماء وبين أن يصلي قائما بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل، وكذا إذا كان كله متنجساً؛ لأن النظر إليهما بسبب للفتنه. (ع)] وقال زفر ومحمد: لزمه أن يصلي فيه بركوع وسجود، ولا يجوز له أن يصلي عرياناً؛ لأن خطاب التطهير سقط عنه لعجزه و لم يسقط عنه خطاب الستر لقدرته عليه، فصار بمنزلة الطاهر في حقه؛ ولأن في الصلاة فيه ترك فرض واحد، وهو طهارة الثوب النجس، وفي الصلاة عرياناً ترك فروض من ستر العورة والقيام والركوع والسجود ، ولنا أن المأمور به الستر بالطاهر، فإذا لم يقدر عليه سقط، فيميل إلى أيها شاء، والجواب عن ترك الفروض أنه وإن صلى قاعداً قد أتى ببدلها، وهو الإيماء، فلا يكون تاركاً لها لقيام البدل مقام الأصل، والأصل في جنس هذه المسألة أن من ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما؛ لأن مباشرة الحرام لا تجوز إلا لضرورة، مثاله: رجل لو قام وركع وسجد ينفلت ريحه، وإن جلس ويؤمئ لا ينفلت فيصلى قاعداً بإيماء؛ لأن ترك القيام والركوع والسجود أهون؛ لأن له عوضاً، وقيد تقيد تركه في بعض الصور كالتطوع على الدابة. (فتح) ولو عدم ثوبا إلخ أراد بالثوب ما يستر عورته، وبالعدم عدم القدرة حتى لو أبيح له ثوب ثبتت القدرة على الأصح، وإذا وعد به ينتظر ، ولو قدر عليه بالشراء بثمن المثل وله ثمنه يلزمه الشراء، وإلا صلى قاعداً مؤمياً؛ لما روى أنس بن مالك أن أصحاب رسول الله الله ركبوا في السفينة فانكسرت بهم السفينة، فخرجوا من البحر عرياناً فصلوا قعوداً بالإيماء، وهذا قول روي عنهم، و لم يرو عن أقرانهم خلاف ذلك، فجعل محل الإجماع. (فتح، مستخلص) ثوباً : أي ساتراً ولو حريراً أو نباتاً أو طيناً يلطخها به. (ط) قاعدا نهارا أو ليلا في بيت أو صحراء. (فتح)
And the heavy 'awrah: it is the anus, penis, and testicles; meaning its ruling is the ruling of the shin in that uncovering a quarter of it prevents. (T) And the enslaved woman: [the full-owned, the mudabbara, the mukataba, and others.] Due to the saying of 'Umar: 'Take off your khimar, O Daffar (i.e. the stinking one), do you imitate free women?' when he saw a slave girl wearing a headcover. The wisdom in forbidding her from imitating free women is that foolish people used to harass slave girls, and 'Umar feared confusion leading to greater fitna. Allah said: 'That is more likely that they will be known and not be harmed' (Quran 33:59). And because she goes out for her master's needs in service clothes usually, so her situation is considered like that of women with mahrams regarding men to avoid hardship. (Fath) Like a man in that her 'awrah is from below her navel to below her knee. (T) And her back and belly: because looking at them is a cause [؟] because they are places of desire besides him, and both the back and belly are desired places. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/537] Also 'awrah, and the side follows the belly. The hermaphrodite slave is like the enslaved woman, the free hermaphrodite is like the free woman. 'And if he finds a garment' etc. meaning if the majority of the quarter is pure, it is more appropriate that his prayer is not valid; because the quarter represents the whole. This applies if he does not find something to remove the impurity or reduce it; then he prays with it and does not repeat, but it is not permissible for him to pray naked. (Fath) 'It is not valid' is his prayer because the quarter has the ruling of the whole, as in ihram. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/50] He has the choice between praying naked sitting with gestures or praying standing with bowing and prostration, and the latter is better. Likewise if the entire garment is impure. (A) Zufar and Muhammad said: He must pray in it with bowing and prostration, and it is not permissible for him to pray naked; because the command to purify fell from him due to inability, but the command to cover did not fall from him because he is able, so it is like pure for him. And because praying in it leaves one obligatory act (purity of garment), while praying naked leaves multiple obligations (covering 'awrah, standing, bowing, prostration). Our evidence: The commanded thing is covering with a pure garment; if he is unable, it falls, so he may choose whichever he wishes. The answer regarding leaving obligations: even if he sits, he has performed their substitute (gesturing), so he is not leaving them because the substitute stands in place of the original. The principle in such matters is that if one faces two afflictions, he chooses the easier of them, because direct commission of what is forbidden is only allowed due to necessity. Example: a man who, if he stands and bows and prostrates, his wind escapes, but if he sits and gestures it does not, then he prays sitting with gestures; because leaving standing, bowing, and prostration is easier since they have substitutes. 'And if he lacks a garment' etc. He means by 'garment' what covers his 'awrah, and by 'lack' inability; so if a garment is loaned to him, ability is established according to the correct view, and if promised, he waits. If he can purchase it at the standard price and has the money, he must buy it; otherwise he prays sitting gesturing, due to the hadith of Anas ibn Malik that the Companions were on a ship that broke, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. This is a narration from them, and no opposition from their peers is reported, so it is considered a locus of consensus. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Garment' i.e. a cover, even if silk, plant material, or mud that he smears on. (T) 'Sitting' day or night, in a house or desert. (Fath)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on conditions of prayer, addressing the 'awrah of enslaved women, the ruling on praying with an impure garment, and what to do if one has no garment. First, it defines the 'heavy 'awrah' (anus, penis, testicles) which have the same quarter rule as the shin. Then the 'awrah of an enslaved woman is stated to be like that of a man: from below navel to below knee. This is derived from the practice of 'Umar who ordered a slave girl to remove her khimar, and supported by Quran 33:59 and the rationale of avoiding fitna and hardship. The back and belly are also considered 'awrah. Next, the passage discusses a situation where one has a garment that is impure: if more than a quarter of it is pure, it is preferable not to pray in it (i.e., prayer is invalid), but if less than a quarter is pure, one has the option to pray naked sitting with gestures or to pray standing in the impure garment. The text mentions a difference between Zufar and Muhammad (the two companions) and Abu Hanifa: Zufar and Muhammad hold that one must pray in the impure garment, as the inability to purify is excused but covering is still possible; Abu Hanifa gives a choice, arguing that the command to cover with pure is impossible, so it falls. The passage then explains that the principle is to choose the easier of two afflictions. Finally, if one has no garment at all (or is unable to obtain one), one prays sitting with gestures (i.e., lowering the head for ruku' and sujud), based on the practice of the Companions who were shipwrecked and prayed naked sitting. This is considered a transmitted consensus. The garment can be any cover, even silk, leaves, or mud.

Key Terms
ثوب نجس (thawb najis): An impure garment; if unable to purify or replace, the Hanafi school gives a choice between praying in it standing or praying naked sitting with gestures.
إيماء (imaa'): Gestures performed while sitting to substitute for bowing and prostration when one cannot perform them normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling for a person who has an impure garment and cannot purify it?
A) He must pray naked sitting with gestures
B) He must pray in the impure garment standing
C) He has a choice between A and B, with B being better
D) He must delay prayer until he finds a pure garment

Key Takeaway
When unable to purify an impure garment, the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) grants a choice between praying in it standing or naked sitting with gestures.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Praying Without Clothing
Ruling on praying without any garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling for a person who has no garment to cover his 'awrah in prayer, and EXPLAIN the evidence from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
Without any garment, pray sitting with gestures — the only fully valid prayer when totally naked.

Imagine being shipwrecked and losing all your clothes. The Companions faced this and established a precedent. This lesson covers the extreme case of total nudity in prayer — when covering is impossible, the obligation shifts to gestures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person has no garment whatsoever to cover his 'awrah. This includes not being able to borrow, buy, or find any covering (e.g., leaves, mud, etc.). The hadith of the shipwrecked Companions is the key evidence.
If he can obtain a covering by purchase at a fair price, he must do so. Only total inability triggers this ruling.
2
State the ruling
He must pray sitting with gestures (imaa') for bowing and prostration. He should not stand or perform full postures, as that would expose his 'awrah more.
This applies whether day or night, in a house or desert.
3
Identify the evidence
The hadith of Anas bin Malik that the Companions, when shipwrecked and naked, prayed sitting with gestures. No one among them disagreed, so this is considered a silent consensus (ijma sukti).
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
4
Note the modern mapping
In modern times, this scenario is rare but could occur in extreme emergencies. The principle that necessity overrides normal obligations applies.
If one can cover at least the navel to knee, he must stand and perform full postures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on conditions of prayer, addressing the 'awrah of enslaved women, the ruling on praying with an impure garment, and what to do if one has no garment. First, it defines the 'heavy 'awrah' (anus, penis, testicles) which have the same quarter rule as the shin. Then the 'awrah of an enslaved woman is stated to be like that of a man: from below navel to below knee. This is derived from the practice of 'Umar who ordered a slave girl to remove her khimar, and supported by Quran 33:59 and the rationale of avoiding fitna and hardship. The back and belly are also considered 'awrah. Next, the passage discusses a situation where one has a garment that is impure: if more than a quarter of it is pure, it is preferable not to pray in it (i.e., prayer is invalid), but if less than a quarter is pure, one has the option to pray naked sitting with gestures or to pray standing in the impure garment. The text mentions a difference between Zufar and Muhammad (the two companions) and Abu Hanifa: Zufar and Muhammad hold that one must pray in the impure garment, as the inability to purify is excused but covering is still possible; Abu Hanifa gives a choice, arguing that the command to cover with pure is impossible, so it falls. The passage then explains that the principle is to choose the easier of two afflictions. Finally, if one has no garment at all (or is unable to obtain one), one prays sitting with gestures (i.e., lowering the head for ruku' and sujud), based on the practice of the Companions who were shipwrecked and prayed naked sitting. This is considered a transmitted consensus. The garment can be any cover, even silk, leaves, or mud.

Key Terms
عدم الثوب (adam al-thawb): Lack of any garment or covering for the 'awrah. Triggers the ruling of praying sitting with gestures.
الإيماء (al-imaa'): Gestures performed while sitting to substitute for bowing and prostration. Used when one cannot perform full postures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the shipwrecked Companions do when they became naked?
A) They prayed standing facing the sea
B) They prayed sitting with gestures
C) They delayed prayer until they found clothes
D) They prayed in the water to hide themselves

Key Takeaway
If no covering is available, the Hanafi school requires sitting with gestures for prayer, based on the Companions' consensus.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Prayer with Gestures for the Sick
Presents Hanafi position on prayer of a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer for a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate, and identify the opposing views of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
For the sick, sitting and gesturing in prayer is better than standing and gesturing.

When illness prevents a person from performing the physical postures of prayer—bowing (rukū') and prostration (sujūd)—the Hanafi school provides a concession. This lesson examines the preferred method: praying while seated and making head gestures (imā') instead of actual movements. It also contrasts the Hanafi position with those of Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being ruled upon is the prayer of a sick person who cannot physically bow and prostrate. The Hanafi school permits this person to pray sitting and make gestures (imā') for rukū' and sujūd.
This is a concession (rukhsah) for hardship.
2
State the Hanafi position
The text states: 'مؤمياً بركوع وسجود عندنا' – gesturing with bowing and prostrating is according to us (the Hanafis). Moreover, it is 'أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود' – better than standing with gestures.
The preferred form is sitting with gestures.
3
Identify the opposing view
Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the sick person must stand and gesture: 'وعند زفر والشافعي: يصلي قائماً بركوع وسجود'.
They consider standing a fundamental requirement even if gestures replace actual movements.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that under the Hanafi view, a sick person may sit during prayer, whereas under the opposing view, he must stand if able. Both agree on making gestures.
The disagreement is about the posture (sitting vs standing), not about the permissibility of gestures.
5
Apply the underlying principle
The Hanafi view prioritizes ease (taysir) and relieving hardship. The ruling is consistent with the Qur'anic principle: 'Allah intends ease for you, not hardship' (2:185).
This is an example of istihsan based on necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤمياً بركوع وسجود، وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود. مؤمياً بركوع وسجود عندنا، وعند زفر والشافعي: يصلي قائماً بركوع وسجود.
Gesturing with bowing and prostrating, and it is better than standing with bowing and prostration. Gesturing with bowing and prostration according to us, and according to Zufar and al-Shafi'i: he prays standing with bowing and prostration.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on how a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate should pray. The Hanafi position is that such a person may pray sitting and make gestures (imā') for rukū' and sujūd, and that this is superior to standing and gesturing. The opposing views of Zufar and al-Shafi'i require him to stand and gesture. The text implies that the Hanafi view is based on the principle of taking the easier option for the sick, as gesturing while sitting better mimics the actual postures.

Key Terms
مؤمياً (imā'an): Gesturing with the head or body for bowing and prostrating instead of actual movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred way for a sick person who cannot bow and prostrate to pray?
A) Standing with gestures for rukū' and sujūd
B) Sitting with gestures for rukū' and sujūd
C) Lying down with gestures
D) Performing the prayer later when able

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits and prefers sitting with gestures for a sick person unable to perform bowing and prostration, prioritizing ease.

Salah — Prayer

Definition and Conditions of Intention in Prayer
Definition of intention, its timing, and the verbal utterance dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of intention as the heart's resolve to enter prayer, explain the requirement that it must precede the opening takbir, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on verbal utterance.

Core Idea
Intention is a condition of the heart, not the tongue, and must be present before the opening takbir without interruption.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the fifth condition of prayer: intention (niyyah). We will examine its definition, the timing requirement relative to the opening takbir, and the dispute over whether verbal utterance is necessary. The Hanafi position, based on consensus and the practice of the Prophet, is that only heart intention is required.

Guided Path
1
Define intention as a condition
Extract the definition from the text: intention is the resolve of the heart (qasd al-qalb) to enter prayer. Note that it is a condition (shart), not a pillar.
The Arabic term is النية.
2
Determine the timing requirement
The intention must precede the opening takbir without a break (bila fasil) that severs continuity. Actions like eating or drinking break it; actions like wudu or walking do not.
The text states that delayed intention after takbir is invalid in the apparent narration.
3
Identify the ruling on verbal utterance
Verbal utterance (talfuz) is of no legal consequence. The heart intention governs, even if the tongue errs. It is considered an innovation (bid'ah), though allowed for those with weak resolve.
The Prophet and the four Imams did not practice verbal utterance.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Compare with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that verbal utterance is necessary. The Hanafi response relies on consensus and the Prophet's practice to refute this.
The practical difference: a Hanafi who only intends in heart is valid.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that heart intention suffices and verbal utterance is not required. This is based on the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and consensus.
Later scholars allowed verbal utterance as a helper for those lacking concentration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنية : أي والشرط الخامس النية، وهي قصد القلب للدخول في الصلاة. (ع، ط) بلا فاصل: أي بين النية والتحريمة والنية هي الإرادة الجازمة للدخول في الصلاة والمتقدمة على التكبير كالقائمة عنده، ولا اعتبار للمتأخرة عن التكبير، وقيل: تصح ما دام في الثناء، وقيل: تصح إذا تقدمت إلى الركوع، وقيل: إلى أن يرفع رأسه، وأما التلفظ فلا عبرة به حتى لو قصد أداء الظهر وجرى على لسانه لعصر يكون شارعا، بل هي بدعة وجعلها بعضهم سيئة فجزم بالكراهة، ولم يثبت عنه لهم من طريق صحيح ولا ضعيف أنه كان يقول عند الافتتاح: أصلي كذا، ولا عن أحد الصحابة والتابعين، ولا عن الأئمة الأربعة، بل المنقول أنه عليها كان إذا قام من للصلاة: كبر، فالتلفظ بدعة، لكن استحسنه المتأخرون في حق من لم تجتمع عزيمته، وكيفيتها أن يقول: اللهم إني أريد صلاة كذا فيسرها لي وتقبلها مني وقال الشافعي: لابد من ذكر اللسان، وهذا القول مردود باتفاق العلماء: على أنه إذا نوى بقلبه و لم يتكلم جاز صلاته، والتلفظ بها مخصوص بالحج لامتداد زمانه وكثرة مشاقه. (فتح) بلا فاصل بينها وبين التحريمة بعمل يمنع الاتصال كالأكل والشرب، والذي لا يمنع الاتصال لا يضر كالوضوء والمشي إلى المسجد لإدراك الجماعة، ولا تعتبر النية المتأخرة عن التكبير في ظاهر الرواية.
And intention: that is, the fifth condition is intention, and it is the resolve of the heart to enter into prayer. Without a break: that is, between the intention and the opening takbir, and intention is the firm will to enter prayer and it precedes the takbir, like the standing one with him, and no consideration is given to what comes after the takbir, and it is said: it is valid as long as it is during the recitation, and it is said: it is valid if it occurs before bowing, and it is said: until he raises his head. As for verbal utterance, it is of no consequence, so much so that if he intends to perform Zuhr and his tongue inadvertently says Asr, he becomes a participant. Rather it is an innovation, and some have deemed it evil and declared it disliked. It is not established from him (Prophet) by any authentic or weak chain that he used to say at the opening: 'I pray such-and-such', nor from any Companion or Successor, nor from the four Imams. Rather the transmitted practice is that when he stood for prayer, he would say the takbir. So verbal utterance is an innovation, but later scholars have deemed it good for those whose resolve is weak. Its manner is to say: 'O Allah, I intend such prayer, make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Al-Shafi'i said: mention with the tongue is necessary, and this statement is refuted by consensus of scholars: that if he intends with his heart and does not speak, his prayer is valid. Verbal utterance is specific to Hajj because of its extended time and many hardships. Without a break between it and the opening takbir, by an action that prevents continuity like eating and drinking. Actions that do not prevent continuity are not harmful, like performing ablution and walking to the mosque to catch the congregation. And a delayed intention after the takbir is not considered in the apparent transmission.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth condition of prayer: intention (niyyah). It is a firm resolve in the heart to enter prayer. The intention must precede the opening takbir without any break that would disconnect it, such as eating or drinking. Actions like walking or performing wudu do not invalidate the continuity. Intention after the takbir is not valid in the apparent narration. The text then addresses the issue of verbal utterance: it is not required and was not practiced by the Prophet or his companions. However, later scholars allowed it for those who cannot concentrate. Al-Shafi'i's view that verbal utterance is necessary is refuted by consensus. Verbal utterance is only recommended for Hajj due to its lengthy and arduous nature.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The resolve of the heart to enter into prayer, distinct from verbal expression.
التلفظ (al-talfuz): Verbally uttering the intention; considered bid'ah in Hanafi school except for those with weak resolve.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer commence and prohibits worldly actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct timing of intention relative to the opening takbir?
A) Intention must be made simultaneously with the takbir
B) Intention must be made before the takbir without a break
C) Intention can be made after the takbir as long as it is before the first bowing
D) Intention can be made anytime during the prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention for prayer is a condition of the heart that must precede the opening takbir, and verbal utterance is not required.

Specification of Prayer in Intention for Fard and Nafl
Explains necessity of specifying the prayer in intention for fard, and sufficiency of general intention for nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when specification of the prayer in intention is required and when a general intention suffices, and apply the ruling to fard, nafl, wajib, and other prayers.

Core Idea
Specifying the prayer in intention is a condition for fard, but a general intention suffices for nafl.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on intention (niyyah) in prayer. It explains that while a general intention of prayer is sufficient for supererogatory acts, obligatory prayers require specifying which prayer one is performing. Understanding this distinction ensures the validity of one's salat according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer category
Determine whether the prayer is fard, wajib, sunnah, or nafl. The rule on specification depends on this category.
Fard and wajib prayers require specification; nafl and sunnah do not (exception: sunnah of Fajr? Generally sunnah mu'akkada is considered sunnah, not wajib, but the text says 'sunnah' and 'nafl' suffice with general intention)
2
Apply the specification rule for fard and wajib
For fard and wajib prayers (including witr, Eid, prostration of recitation, two rak'ahs of tawaf), the person must specify which prayer (e.g., Zuhr, Asr) and intend its obligation or necessity.
General intention like 'I intend to pray' is not enough because the attribute of obligation must be intended.
3
Check special cases
For the funeral prayer (janazah), one intends that it is fard and supplication for the deceased. For a follower (muqtadi), one must also intend following the imam.
The Meccan must face the exact Ka'bah; for others, facing the direction suffices.
4
Note the subordinate nature of rak'ah count
The number of rak'ahs is subordinate to the specification of the prayer; if one intends Fajr as four rak'ahs, it suffices because the specification of Fajr overrides the mistaken number.
Thus, specifying the prayer itself is key, not the rak'ah count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرط أن يعلم بقلبه أي صلاة يصلي، ويكفيه مطلق النية للنفل والسنة والتراويح، وللفرض شرط تعيينه كالعصر مثلا، والمقتدي ينوي المتابعة أيضاً، وللجنازة ينوي أي فرض كان أي تعيين أنه فرض الصلاة لله تعالى والدعاء للميت، واستقبال القبلة، فللمكي فرضه إصابة عينها، والمنذور أي ينوي الكعبة للفرض: أي ما لزم في ذمّة، سواء كان فرضاً ولو قضاء أو غيره كما أفسده من النفل وسجود التلاوة والوتر وصلاة العيدين وركعتي الطواف، فلا يكفي لها نية مطلق الصلاة؛ لأن الفرضية والوجوب صفة زائدة، فلابد أن ينويها؛ لأن وقتها ظرف صالح للفرض والنفل كليهما، فما لم يعين لا يحكم عليه بالفرضية، فينوي فرض الوقت أو ظهر الوقت إلا في الجمعة للاختلاف في فرضها، وأعداد الركعات تابعة لتعيين الصلاة، فعلى هذا لو نوى الفجر أربعاً والظهر ثنتين أجزأه وكذا استقبال القبلة على الأصح.
And the condition is that he knows in his heart which prayer he is praying, and a general intention suffices for nafl, sunnah, and tarawih. For fard, specification is a condition, e.g., Asr. The follower must also intend following [the imam]. For the funeral prayer, he intends whatever fard it is, i.e., he specifies that it is the fard prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased. And facing the qibla: for the Meccan, his duty is to face the exact Ka'bah. The vowed prayer: he intends the Ka'bah for fard: i.e., whatever has become obligatory in his liability, whether fard even if make-up or other, such as when he nullified a nafl or recitation of prostration, witr, the two Eid prayers, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. For these, a general intention of prayer does not suffice because fardiyyah and wujub are additional attributes; so he must intend them. Because its time is a container suitable for both fard and nafl, so unless he specifies, it is not judged as fard. So he intends fard of the time or Zuhr of time, except for Jumu'ah due to difference in its fard status. The numbers of rak'ahs are subordinate to the specification of the prayer. So based on this, if he intends Fajr as four and Zuhr as two, it suffices. And similarly facing the qibla on the correct opinion.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage elaborates the requirement of specifying the prayer in intention. For supererogatory prayers (nafl, sunnah, tarawih), a general intention of prayer is sufficient because their essence is the same as prayer. For obligatory prayers (fard), one must specify which prayer, e.g., Fajr or Zuhr, because the attribute of obligation is an added quality that must be intended. The same applies to other obligatory prayers like witr, Eid, prostration of recitation, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. The follower (muqtadi) must also intend to follow the imam. For the funeral prayer, one intends the fard and supplication for the deceased. The specification of rak'ah counts is not necessary; they follow the specification of prayer. So if someone intends Fajr as four rak'ahs, it is still valid.

Key Terms
تعيين الصلاة (ta'yin al-salah): Specifying which prayer one is performing (e.g., Zuhr, Asr) in intention.
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): A general intention of prayer without specifying type or time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of prayer is a general intention (without specifying the prayer) sufficient according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard prayers
B) Wajib prayers like Witr
C) Nafl and sunnah prayers
D) Make-up prayers (qada)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires specifying the prayer in intention for fard and wajib prayers, but a general intention suffices for nafl and sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions of Intention in Prayer: Specification and Following
Ruling on intention conditions with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of intention in prayer and explain when specification (ta'yin) is required, including for the follower and funeral prayer.

Core Idea
Intention is the heart of prayer, but for fard, you must specify the exact prayer—except when following an imam, where following alone suffices.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on intention (niyyah) in prayer. While intention is a condition for all prayers, the classical texts distinguish between obligatory and supererogatory acts, and between praying alone or behind an imam. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies what must be specified and when a follower's general intention is enough.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is establishing intention for prayer. Intention (niyyah) is a condition (shart) for validity, not a pillar (rukn).
This is a difference from some other schools that consider intention a rukn.
2
Identify the condition for fard prayer
For an obligatory prayer (fard), specification (ta'yin) of the particular prayer (e.g., Dhuhr, Asr) is a condition. Without specification, the prayer does not count as that fard.
The time is suitable for both fard and nafl, hence specification is needed to determine which is intended.
3
Examine the exception for the follower
A follower (muqtadi) does not need to specify the prayer if he intends to follow the imam. The intention to follow (niyyat al-iqtida') suffices for specification on the soundest view.
The follower must have three intentions: intention of prayer, specification, and following. But following can substitute for specification.
4
Apply to funeral prayer
For funeral prayer (salat al-janaza), one must intend it as an obligatory prayer for Allah and specify that it is for the deceased. The specification is needed because it is an obligation.
Verbal utterance is recommended but not required; intention is in the heart.
5
Note the subsidiary ruling on rak'ahs
The number of rak'ahs is subsidiary to the specification of the prayer. If one specifies the correct prayer but intends wrong rak'ahs, the prayer is valid on the soundest view.
Example: intending Fajr as four rak'ahs is valid because the specification (Fajr) is correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب شروط الصلاة
ينوي الصلاة ومتابعة إمامه
وللفرض شرط تعيينه كالعصر مثلا، والمقتدي ينوي المتابعة أيضاً، وللجنازة ينوي أي فرض كان أي تعيين أنه فرض الصلاة لله تعالى والدعاء للميت،
والمنذور
أي ينوي
أي السادس من الشرط استقبال إلخ المشاهدة للكعبة
الكعبة
للفرض: أي ما لزم في ذمّة، سواء كان فرضاً ولو قضاء أو غيره كما أفسده من النفل وسجود التلاوة والوتر وصلاة العيدين وركعتي الطواف، فلا يكفي لها نية مطلق الصلاة؛ لأن الفرضية والوجوب صفة زائدة، فلابد أن ينويها؛ لأن وقتها ظرف صالح للفرض والنفل كليهما، فما لم يعين لا يحكم عليه بالفرضية، فينوي فرض الوقت أو ظهر الوقت إلا في الجمعة للاختلاف في فرضها، وأعداد الركعات تابعة لتعيين الصلاة، فعلى هذا لو نوى الفجر أربعاً والظهر ثنتين أجزأه وكذا استقبال القبلة على الأصح. (فتح، مستخلص) كالعصر مثلا: بأن يعين فرض العصر الحاضر، ولو نوى فرض الوقت يجوز ، ولا يشترط نية أعداد الركعات. (مسكين) والمقتدي إلخ لأنه يلزمه الفساد من جهة إمامه، فلابد من التزامه. أيضاً: نصب على المصدر يقال: "آض أيضاً إذا رجع، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لابد للمقتدي من ثلاث نيات: نية أصل الصلاة ونية التعيين ونية الاقتداء، وأن نية الاقتداء تكفيه عن التعيين حتى لو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام أو الشروع في صلاة الإمام ولم يعين الصلاة جاز على الأصح، بخلاف ما إذا نوى صلاة الإمام ولم يعين الصلاة جاز على الأصح، بخلاف ما إذا نوى صلاة الإمام ولم ينو الاقتداء لا يجزئه؛ لأنه تعيين لصلاة الإمام وليس باقتداء له، وأفاد أن تعيين الإمام ليس بشرط، فلو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام بظن أنه زيد فإذا هو عمرو صح، ولو نوى الاقتداء بزيد فإذا هو عمرو فإنه لا يصح، ولو رأى شخصه فنوى الاقتداء بهذا الإمام جاز؛ لأنه عرفه بالإشارة، وكذا لو عرفه بمكان كالقائم في المحراب، وقيد بالمقتدي؛ لأن الإمام لا يشترط لصحة اقتداء الرجال به نية الإمامة، وفي حق النساء لابد أن ينوي إمامتهن. (فتح) للميّت لأنه الواجب عليه، فيجب تعيينه وإخلاصه الله تعالى، ويقول بلسانه أصلي الله تعالى داعياً للميت. [رمز الحقائق: ٥١/١]
Chapter of Conditions of Prayer. He intends the prayer and following his imam. For the obligatory prayer, specifying it is a condition, such as Asr for example. The follower also intends following. For the funeral prayer, he intends whatever obligatory prayer it is, i.e., specifying that it is the obligatory prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased. ... [commentary] For the obligatory: that which is binding in the liability, whether it is an obligation even if make-up or other like what he corrupted from supererogatory, prostration of recitation, witr, Eid prayers, and two rak'ahs of tawaf. So absolute intention of prayer is not sufficient, because obligatory and wajib are additional attributes, so he must intend them; because the time is suitable for both obligatory and supererogatory, so without specification it is not ruled as obligatory. So he intends the obligatory of the time or dhuhr of the time, except in Jumu'ah due to disagreement on its being obligatory. Numbers of rak'ahs are subsidiary to the specification of the prayer. So if he intended Fajr as four and Dhuhr as two, it suffices him, and likewise facing the qiblah according to the most sound. ... The follower: because corruption is binding from the side of his imam, so he must commit to it. ... He must have three intentions: intention of the prayer itself, intention of specification, intention of following. The intention of following suffices for specification. ... For the deceased: because it is obligatory upon him, so he must specify and devote it to Allah, and say with his tongue 'I pray to Allah, supplicating for the deceased.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement on the conditions of intention in prayer. It opens with the matn stating that for an obligatory prayer, specifying the prayer (ta'yin) is a condition. The commentary explains that intention is a condition (shart) for validity, not a pillar. For obligatory prayers, the general intention of prayer does not suffice because the time is shared between obligatory and supererogatory; so one must intend, for example, 'the obligatory of Dhuhr'. However, for prayers like Jumu'ah, there is flexibility due to ikhtilaf. The follower (muqtadi) must additionally intend to follow the imam; this intention can substitute for specification. The follower does not need to specify the prayer if he intends to follow the imam, even if he mistakes the imam's identity, provided he intends the person he sees. The imam himself does not need to intend leading men, but women must intend leading women. For funeral prayer, one must intend the prayer for the deceased and specify it as an obligation regardless of which type. This passage also notes that the number of rak'ahs is subsidiary to the specification, so if one intends the wrong number but specifies the correct prayer, it is valid.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention of the heart to perform the prayer, a condition for validity.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specifying the particular prayer (e.g., Dhuhr, Asr) in intention.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer, who must intend to follow the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower intends to pray behind the imam but does not specify the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) It is valid because following suffices for specification.
C) It is valid only if he verbally states the prayer.
D) It is invalid unless the imam specifies the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for prayer; for fard, specification is required, but following the imam can replace that specification.

Facing the Qiblah: Obligation and Exceptions
Rulings and proofs on facing the qiblah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of facing the qiblah, distinguish the rulings for Meccans, non-Meccans, and the fearful, and apply the correct ijtihad rule when the qiblah is obstructed.

Core Idea
Facing the qiblah is fard, but its degree depends on ability: exact Kaaba for Meccans, direction for others, any direction for the fearful.

The qiblah is the direction of the Kaaba, established by Quranic command. However, the obligation is not absolute; it accommodates different levels of ability. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings for three categories: the Meccan who can see the Kaaba, the one whose view is obstructed, and the one who cannot face it at all due to fear or illness. The underlying principle is that Allah does not charge a soul beyond its capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary act and its proof
Read the Quranic verse (2:144) cited in the text. The imperative 'fawallū' indicates obligation, and 'shatrahu' specifies the direction. The proof establishes that facing the qiblah is a fard condition for prayer.
The verse commands 'turn your faces toward it', which the Hanafi school interprets as a binding instruction.
2
Distinguish the ruling for the Meccan with direct sight
For a Meccan actually in Mecca with unobstructed view, the obligation is to face the exact Kaaba itself (ʿayn al-Kaʿba). This is by consensus.
The text says 'hitting its very entity' (iṣābat ʿaynihā).
3
Analyze the exception for the Meccan with a building
If a Meccan is inside a house such that walls block the view, the ruling is like that of an absent person (ghāʾib). He must perform ijtihad to determine the direction, and if later his error becomes apparent, he does not repeat the prayer because he did what was within his capacity.
The text prefers this as 'al-aṣaḥḥ' (most sound), indicating a tarjīḥ within the school.
4
Explain the ruling for non-Meccans
For anyone not in Mecca, the obligation is to face the direction of the Kaaba (jihatuhā), not the exact structure. This is the sound position according to the text.
ʿAyn explains 'hitting its direction' means facing the direction of the Kaaba.
5
Describe the concession for the fearful and excused
A person who has a valid excuse—such as fear of an enemy or predator, severe illness, or being on a ship at sea without means to determine the qiblah—may pray in any direction. The rationale is that the true objective is to turn to Allah, and the Kaaba is only a test; when inability is realized, the test is fulfilled by any direction.
This applies to the sick who cannot be turned, one on a board in the sea, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستقبال القبلة أي لغير الخائف وهو استفعال من قبلت الماشية الوادي يعني قابلته وليس السين فيه للطلب؛ لأن الشرط المقصود بالذات المقابلة، لا طلبها فاستفعل بمعنى فعل والقبلة في الأصل الحالة التي يقابل الشيء عليها غيره، ثم صارت كالعلم فلجهة التي تستقبل للصلاة سميت بذلك؛ لأن الناس يقابلونها، وتسمى محراباً أيضاً لمحاربة النفس والشيطان عندها. (فتح) القبلة: لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ﴾ (البقرة: ١٤٤) أي جهته. (ع) فللمكي: تفسير لقوله: "واستقبال القبلة"، حتى لو صلى مكي في بيته في مكة ينبغي أن يصلي بحيث لو أزيل الجدران يقع استقباله على جهة الكعبة، لكن الأصح إن حكم من كان بينه وبينها بناء حكم الغائب حتى إذا اجتهد وصلى وبان خطؤه لا يعيد؛ لأنه أتى بما في وسعه فلا يكلف بما زاد عليه. (مسكين، فتح) فرضه: أي فرض الاستقبال. إصابة عينها : أي التوجه إلى عين الكعبة إجماعاً. ولغيره إصابة جهتها، والخائف يصلّى إلى أي جهة قدر (ع) إصابة جهتها: أي التوجه إلى جهة الكعبة في الصحيح (ع) والخائف : أي من له عذر يمنع من التوجه إليها، سواء سبع، إن صلى إلى جهة الكعبة أو لا كعدم الاستطاعة على التوجه إليها لضعف مرض أو أو من غيره، ولا يجد من يوجهه إليها، والفقه فيه أن المصلي في خدمة الله تعالى فلابد من الإقبال عليه، وهو منزه عن الجهة، فابتلاه بالتوجه إلى الكعبة، فلما اعتراه الخوف تحقق العذر ، فأشبه حالة الاشتباه في تحقق العذر، فيتوجه إلى أي جهة قدر؛ لأن الكعبة لم تعبد لعينها حتى لو سجد لها كفي بل للابتلاء وهو حاصل بذلك. (فتح) أي جهة قدر : لتحقق العجز، وكذا المريض إذا لم يجد من يحوله إليها ومن كان على خشبة في البحر. (ع)
And facing the qiblah – for other than the fearful. It is istif'al from 'qabalat al-mashiyah al-wadi', meaning he faced it, and the sin is not for seeking; because the condition intended essentially is the facing, not seeking it. So istif'al is in the meaning of fa'ala. And al-qiblah originally is the state upon which something faces another, then it became a proper noun for the direction faced in prayer, so named because people face it. It is also called mihrab for fighting the self and the devil. (Fath) al-Qiblah: due to His statement: 'So turn your faces toward it' (2:144) i.e., its direction. (Ayn) So for the Meccan: interpretation of his statement: 'And facing the qiblah', so if a Meccan prays in his house in Mecca, he should pray such that if walls were removed, his facing would be toward the Kaaba. But the sound position is that the ruling of one who has a building between him and it is the ruling of the absent, so if he exercises ijtihad and prays and his error becomes apparent, he does not repeat, because he did what was in his capacity and is not charged beyond that. (Miskin, Fath) His fard: i.e., the obligation of facing. 'Hitting its very entity' means facing the very Kaaba by consensus. And for other than him, hitting its direction. And the fearful prays to whatever direction he can. (Ayn) 'Hitting its direction' means facing the direction of the Kaaba according to the sound view. (Ayn) And the fearful: the one with an excuse preventing him from facing it, whether a lion, if he prays facing the Kaaba or not, like inability to face it due to weakness from illness or other, and he does not find one to direct him. The fiqh is that the worshiper is in servitude to Allah, so he must turn to Him, and He is free from direction, so He tested him by facing the Kaaba. When fear overcomes him, the excuse is realized, so it resembles the case of ambiguity in realization of excuse, so he turns to whatever direction he can, because the Kaaba was not worshipped for its own sake – even if he prostrated to it, it would suffice – but rather for the test, which is achieved by that. (Fath) 'To whatever direction he can' due to realization of inability, and likewise the sick person if he does not find one to turn him toward it, and one on a board in the sea. (Ayn)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on facing the qiblah. It begins by defining the condition of facing the qiblah, noting that it is the direction faced in prayer, and derives from the attribute of facing. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:144) commanding to turn faces toward the Sacred Mosque. The commentary then distinguishes between the Meccan resident and others: for a Meccan with direct sight of the Kaaba, it is fard to face the actual Kaaba; if there is a building obstructing, he must use ijtihad and does not repeat if wrong, like an absent person. For non-Meccans, facing the direction is sufficient. The passage then covers the fearful (khā'if): one who cannot face the qiblah due to fear or illness may pray in any direction because the true purpose is worship and submission, not the physical direction itself. This relaxation is due to inability, similar to the ambiguity case. The ruling extends to the sick who cannot be turned and one on a boat at sea.

Key Terms
قبلة (qiblah): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca that must be faced during prayer.
استقبال (istiqbāl): The act of facing the qiblah; a condition for prayer.
محراب (mihrāb): A niche in the mosque indicating the qiblah; also called mihrab for struggling against the self and devil.
إصابة جهة (iṣābat jiha): Facing the direction of the Kaaba, not the exact structure.
خائف (khā'if): One who fears for his life or safety, excused from facing the qiblah.

B) He does not repeat because he performed ijtihad and did what he could.
C) He must perform ijtihad and then repeat if wrong.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to face the qiblah is conditioned by ability; the underlying purpose is obedience and worship, not the physical structure.

Prayer When Qiblah is Ambiguous: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Repeating Prayer After Error
Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on repeating prayer when qiblah error is discovered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that prayer performed after ijtihad for qiblah is valid even if the direction is later discovered to be wrong, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
If you did your best to find the qiblah, your prayer is valid — obligation is limited by capacity.

When the qiblah direction is unknown and no one can tell you, the Hanafi school requires you to perform ijtihad (taharrī) to find the most likely direction. But what happens if you later discover you were facing the wrong way? This lesson examines the dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is: the Hanafis say your prayer is valid regardless, while the Shafi'is require repetition if your error is certain. We will walk through the proofs and reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Determine when taharrī becomes required: when the qiblah is ambiguous and no knowledgeable person is present to ask.
If a knowledgeable person is available, inquiry (su'al) is obligatory, not ijtihad.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
If after performing taharrī and praying, a person later discovers the qiblah direction was wrong, the prayer is not repeated. The obligation was on ijtihad, not absolute correctness.
This is the position labeled 'al-ashah' (the soundest) in the text.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if error becomes certain (especially if one turned his back, istidbār), the prayer must be repeated, because error is now certain.
The Shafi'i analogizes to praying before the time based on a mistaken estimation of the time.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on the principle 'al-taklīf muqayyad bi al-wus'' (obligation is limited by capacity). In the time analogy, the person could have asked someone; here no one is available. Also, the qiblah itself can change (as in riding or fear prayer), so error is excusable.
The Hanafi proof also includes Quran 2:115.
5
Examine the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is Quran 2:115 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah', which was revealed for this situation. This indicates that any direction is acceptable when one is genuinely unsure and has performed ijtihad.
The dalal is zanni (speculative) but strong enough to support the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة تحرى، وإن أخطأ لم يعد، أي من عجز عن استقبال القبلة و لم يكن عنده من ! يسأله يعني من أهل ذلك المكان بحيث لو صاح به سمعه، فحينئذ يتحرى، ولو كان شخص واقف عليها حاضراً لم يجز التحري بل يلزمه السؤال؛ لأن الاستخبار فوق التحري، فلا يصار إلى الأدنى مع إمكان المصير إلى الأعلى، فإن كان من أهله لا يقلده؛ لأن حاله مثل حاله والتحري تبعية الظن الغالب، سواء كان في مسجد أو في مفازة أو في مسجد محلة أخرى ولا محراب له، أما إذا اشتبهت عليه في بيته فلا يتحرى. (فتح) تحرى: أي يطلب ما هو أوقع بقلبه وأحرى من غيره، فيصلي إلى أي جهة مال إليها ظنه؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ الله (البقرة: ١١٥) نزلت في الصلاة حالة الاشتباه كما أخرجه الترمذي، فلو صلى من اشتبهت عليه حالها بلا تحرّ أعادها لترك ما افترض عليه من التحري، إلا إذا علم أنه أصاب بعد الفراغ لحصول المقصود. (فتح) تحرى: أي اجتهد وهو بذل المجهود في نيل المقصود، ولا يجوز التحري بوجود الأعلام أو العالم بها. (ع) وإن أخطأ : يعني إذا صلى إلى جهة تحريه وعلم بعد الفراغ أن جهة القبلة كانت غيرها لا تجب عليه الإعادة وهو الأصح؛ لأن ما لزم في ذمته هو التحري ولم يقصر في ذلك، وقال الشافعي: يعيد إن استدبر أي ظهر استدباره بعد الفراغ؛ لأن خطأه ظهر بيقين فصار كما لو صلى الفرض قبل دخول وقت على ظن أنه دخل، ولنا أن التكليف مقيد بالوسع وليس في وسعه إلا التوجه إلى جهة التحري بخلاف ما ذكر؛ لأنه يمكنه السؤال ممن هو مطلع على حال الوقت، ولأن القبلة تقبل الانتقال من جهة إلى جهة كما في حالة الركوب والخوف، فكذا حالة الاشتباه فلا يعيد. (فتح) لم يعد : أي الصلاة وقال الشافعي: يعيد إن استدبر لتيقنه بالخطأ، قلنا: التكليف مقيد بالوسع وقد أتى بما في وسعه. (ع)
And whoever the qiblah is ambiguous to him, he makes ijtihad (taharrī), and if he errs he does not repeat. i.e., whoever is unable to face the qiblah and does not have someone to ask, meaning from the people of that place such that if he called out he would hear him, then he makes ijtihad. If there is a person present who knows it, ijtihad is not allowed; rather he must ask, because inquiry is above ijtihad, so one does not resort to the lower when the higher is possible. If the person is one of the locals, he does not blindly follow him, because his situation is like his own; and ijtihad follows the dominant conjecture, whether in a mosque or desert or mosque of another locality without a mihrab. As for when it is ambiguous in his house, he does not make ijtihad. (Fath) Taharrī: he seeks what is most likely in his heart and more worthy than others, and prays to whichever direction his conjecture inclines. Due to His statement: 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115), revealed for prayer in the state of ambiguity as recorded by al-Tirmidhi. So if one for whom the situation is ambiguous prays without ijtihad, he repeats it for abandoning what was made obligatory upon him of ijtihad, unless he knows after finishing that he was correct, due to attainment of the purpose. (Fath) Taharrī: he strives, exerting effort to reach the goal, and ijtihad is not permissible when there are signs or someone who knows it. (Ayn) 'And if he errs': meaning if he prays to the direction of his ijtihad and learns after finishing that the qiblah direction was otherwise, repetition is not obligatory on the soundest view, because what was binding upon him was the ijtihad, and he did not fall short in that. Al-Shafi'i said: He repeats if he turned his back, i.e., it becomes clear that he turned his back after finishing, because his error became certain, so it is like praying an obligatory prayer before the time on the assumption that it had entered. Our argument: The obligation is limited by capacity, and he had no capacity except to face the direction of his ijtihad, unlike the mentioned case because he could ask someone aware of the time. And because the qiblah is subject to change from one direction to another, as in the case of riding and fear, so similarly in the case of ambiguity, he does not repeat. (Fath) 'He does not repeat' meaning the prayer. And al-Shafi'i said: He repeats if he turned his back due to certainty of error. We said: Obligation is limited by capacity, and he did what was in his capacity. (Ayn)
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is an inter_madhhab_dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether one must repeat prayer if, after performing ijtihad to find the qiblah, it becomes clear that the direction was wrong. The matn states that if the qiblah is ambiguous, one must perform taharrī (ijtihad), and if he errs he does not repeat. The commentary elaborates that one must first inquire if a knowledgeable person is available; if not, taharrī is obligatory. If he prays without taharrī, the prayer must be repeated unless he accidentally faces correctly. The Hanafi proof includes the Quranic verse (2:115) and the principle that obligation is within capacity (at-taklīf muqayyad bi al-wus'). The Shafi'i argument is that error becomes certain, so repetition is required like praying before time based on mistaken estimation. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the time case, one can ask, but here there is no one, and the qiblah itself is subject to change (as in riding or fear). The text affirms the Hanafi position as the soundest (al-ashah).

Key Terms
تحرى (taharrī): To seek the most likely direction of the qiblah through personal effort (ijtihad) when it is ambiguous.
اشتباه (ishtibāh): Ambiguity or lack of clarity regarding the qiblah direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person prays after performing taharrī for the qiblah and later discovers he was facing exactly opposite (istidbār), what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) He does not repeat because he fulfilled the obligation of taharrī.
C) He must repeat only if he was in a mosque.
D) He must repeat and also make a sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when the qiblah is ambiguous, the obligation shifts to ijtihad; if you perform it sincerely, your prayer is valid even if later discovered wrong.

Turning to Correct Qibla During Prayer
Ruling on correcting qibla during prayer and group prayer with uncertain direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on correcting qibla direction during prayer and apply it to scenarios of individual and congregational prayer.

Core Idea
If you realize the qibla was wrong during prayer, turn immediately and continue — no restart needed.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: discovering a qibla error during prayer does not invalidate the prayer. You will learn the proof from the Prophet's approval of the Ansar of Quba' and how this applies to individuals and congregations when the qibla is uncertain. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary repetition of prayers and clarifies the role of ijtihad (taharri) in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is turning to the correct qibla during prayer. What is the hukm level? The Hanafi school holds that turning is wajib; the prayer remains valid without restart.
The ruling applies whether the error is discovered early or late in the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the story of the Ansar in Masjid Quba' who turned from Jerusalem to Mecca during prayer upon hearing the abrogation of the qibla. The Prophet approved their action, establishing the ruling.
This is a sunnah ahad, muttafaq alayh (agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's approval indicates permissibility and correctness of turning during prayer without restarting. The act of turning itself is a valid adjustment, not an invalidation.
The dalala is zanni (probative) but sufficient for a wajib ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require restarting the prayer if the error is discovered early, viewing the initial direction as invalidating the first rak'ah. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the Quba' incident.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the prayer is valid without restart.
5
Apply to congregational prayer with taharri
When a group prays in darkness, each performing ijtihad, their prayer is valid even if directions differ from the imam, as long as each follows his own belief. However, if one is certain the imam's direction is wrong, he cannot follow him.
The measure is the individual's belief (i'tiqad); see the case of praying inside the Ka'bah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن علم به في صلاته استدار. ولو تحرى قوم جهات، وجهلوا حال إمامهم يجزيهم. فإن علم به بأن أخبره من هو عالم بحالها أو بعلامات أخر، وهو في الصلاة يجب عليه أن يتحول من ساعته في الصلاة وليس عليه أن يستأنف، والأصل في هذه المسألة قصة الأنصار بمسجد قباء وتحولهم في الصلاة إلى القبلة، واستحسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فعلهم، ومن لم يقع تحريه على شيء صلى لكل جهة مرة، وفي إطلاق كلام المصنف إشارة إلى أنه لو علم بالخطأ استدار، وإن كان بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد أو في سجود السهو. (فتح) استدار: أي إلى القبلة وأتم؛ لأن أهل قباء لما بلغهم نسخ القبلة استداروا في الصلاة كهيئتهم. (ع) ولو تحرى قوم إلخ : أي لو صلى قوم في ليلة مظلمة وتحروا القبلة وتوجه كل إلى جهة تحريه، ولم يعلم أحد أن الإمام إلى أي جهة توجه لكن يعلم كل واحد أن الإمام ليس خلفه جازت صلاتهم؛ لأن كلاً منهم استقبل جهة تحريه وإن خالف جهتهم لجهة الإمام كما في جوف الكعبة، أما لو علم جهة الإمام وظن أن الإمام أخطأ القبلة تصح صلاته، فالمعتبر في الصحة والفساد اعتقاده، فلو اتحد جهة تحريه بجهة إمامه في زعمه جازت، ولو اختلفتا في زعمه لم تجز. (فتح) قوم أي جماعة مع الإمام عند اشتباه القبلة. (ع) يجزيهم تلك الصلاة إذا كانوا خلف الإمام؛ لأن القبلة في حقهم جهة التحرى، ومن تيقن منهم مخالفة إمامه في الجهة أو تقدمه عليه حالة الأداء لم تجز صلاته؛ لأنه اعتقد إمامه على الخطأ في الأولى وترك فرض المقام في الثانية. (ع)
If he realizes it [the qibla error] during his prayer, he turns around. And if a group [of people] perform ijtihad [to determine the qibla] in different directions, and they are ignorant of the state of their imam, it suffices them. If he realizes it through someone who knows its direction or through other signs, and he is in the prayer, it is obligatory upon him to turn from the moment he is in the prayer, and he does not have to start anew. The basis for this issue is the story of the Ansar in the mosque of Quba' and their turning during prayer to the qibla, and the Prophet's approval of their action. And the one whose ijtihad does not result in any direction should pray once towards each direction. In the absolute wording of the author, there is an indication that if he realizes the error, he turns, even if it is after sitting for the extent of the tashahhud or during the prostration of forgetfulness. (Fath) 'He turns': i.e., to the qibla and completes [the prayer]; because when the people of Quba' received the abrogation of the qibla, they turned in their prayer as they were. (Ayni) 'And if a group...etc.': i.e., if a group of people pray on a dark night and they perform ijtihad for the qibla, and each faces the direction of his ijtihad, and no one knows which direction the imam faced, but each one knows that the imam is not behind him, their prayer is permissible; because each of them faced the direction of his ijtihad, even if their direction differed from the imam's direction, as in the case of the interior of the Ka'bah. However, if he knows the imam's direction and thinks that the imam missed the qibla, his prayer is valid, for what counts for validity and invalidity is his belief. So if his ijtihad direction coincides with his imam's direction in his estimation, it is permissible; and if they differ in his estimation, it is not permissible. (Fath) 'A group': i.e., a congregation with the imam when the qibla is confused. (Ayni) 'It suffices them': that prayer when they are behind the imam, because the qibla for them is the direction of ijtihad. And whoever among them is certain of his imam's opposition in direction or his being ahead of him in the performance, his prayer is not valid; because he believes his imam to be in error in the first case, and he abandons the obligation of standing in the second case. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on conditions of prayer addresses the situation where a person discovers that the direction he is facing for prayer is not the true qibla. The ruling is clear: if while in prayer he learns of the correct qibla, he must turn immediately and complete the prayer from that point; he does not have to restart. The proof cited is the incident of the Ansar in the mosque of Quba' who were praying towards Jerusalem and then received news of the change of qibla towards Mecca; they turned in their prayer and the Prophet approved. The commentator (Fath) explains that this turning is necessary even if it occurs late in the prayer, such as after the tashahhud or during sujud al-sahw. The passage then discusses a situation where a group of people, along with their imam, are uncertain of the qibla in darkness and each makes an independent ijtihad. The ruling is that their prayer is valid as long as each worships according to his own ijtihad, even if their directions differ from the imam, similar to praying inside the Ka'bah where all directions are valid. If one knows the imam's direction but believes the imam is mistaken, his prayer is still valid because the measure is his own belief. However, if he is certain that the imam's direction conflicts with his own ijtihad, then his prayer is invalid because he believes the imam is in error. In such a case, he cannot follow the imam. The commentator (Ayni) adds that for those behind the imam who are unaware of the imam's direction, the qibla for them is the direction they themselves settle upon through ijtihad. But if one is certain that the imam is facing a different direction or is ahead of him in the prayer, then his own prayer is invalid due to his belief that the imam is mistaken or due to prematurely following the imam.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharri): The act of making ijtihad or exertion to determine the correct direction of the qibla when it is unclear.
استدارة (istidarah): Turning around to face the correct qibla during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person realizes during prayer that he is facing the wrong qibla, what is the required action?
A) He must stop the prayer and restart from the beginning
B) He must turn to the correct qibla immediately and continue the prayer
C) He should complete the prayer as is and repeat it later with the correct direction
D) He should perform sajdah al-sahw and then turn

Key Takeaway
Discovering a qibla error during prayer does not invalidate the prayer; one must turn to the correct direction immediately and continue, based on the Prophet's approval of the Ansar's action at Quba'.

The Five Fards of Prayer: Takbir, Qiyam, Qira'ah, Ruku, Sujud
Enumeration of five fards with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five fards of prayer according to the Hanafi school, identify the Quranic proof for each, and distinguish between a rukn and a wajib.

Core Idea
The five fards of prayer are takbirat al-ihram, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku, and sujud, each proven by a direct Quranic command.

In this opening of the chapter on prayer description, the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq enumerates the essential pillars (fards) that constitute the prayer's structure. Understanding these five components is foundational because their absence invalidates the prayer entirely. The passage also introduces a conceptual framework for analyzing any act of worship, which helps clarify the difference between essence, pillar, condition, and cause.

Guided Path
1
List the Five Fards
Start by reading the first line: 'Its fard are: the takbirat al-ihram, standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.' Memorize this list as the core pillars.
The text also mentions that the fards are seven, but only five are listed here; the other two (likely qa'dah) appear later.
2
Find the Quranic Proof for Each
For each fard, the commentary cites a Quranic verse: takbir (Muddaththir:3), qiyam (Baqarah:238), qira'ah (Muzzammil:20), ruku and sujud (Hajj:77). The imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The proof for qira'ah is absolute, not specific to al-Fatiha.
3
Understand Key Details
Note the distinctions: standing is a pillar only in fard prayers; recitation is any portion of the Quran; bowing requires only the minimum bending; prostration requires forehead and feet, and the nose suffices as part of the face.
Additions beyond the minimum are wajib or sunnah, not fard.
4
Apply the Six-Fold Framework
The commentary introduces six aspects for any act: essence, pillar, ruling, locus, condition, cause. Apply this to prayer: essence = salah, pillars = the five fards, locus = mukallaf, conditions = purification etc., ruling = validity/invalidity/reward, cause = times.
This framework helps systematically analyze any act of worship.
5
Distinguish Rukn from Wajib
The passage defines 'fard' as that which is established by definitive proof, and for bowing it says 'the pillar is the minimum; any addition is wajib or mustahabb.' This illustrates the Hanafi hierarchy: omission of a rukn invalidates, omission of a wajib requires sajdah al-sahw.
Not all components of prayer are equal; knowing the rank affects validity and compensation.

باب صفة الصلاة فرضها التحريمة والقيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود أي فرض الصلاة سبعة باب صفة الصلاة: أي في بيان صفتها والصفة: الإمارة اللازمة للشيء. صفة الصلاة : شروع في المشروط بعد بيان الشرط والإضافة فيه كإضافة الجزء إلى الكل، والمراد تبيين الصلاة وكشف ماهيتها، فالإضافة لأدنى ملابسة والصفة والوصف مصدران كالوعد والعدة. واعلم أنه يشترط لثبوت الشيء ستة أشياء: العين وهي ماهية الشيء، والركن وهو جزء الماهية، والحكم وهو إثبات الأثر الثابت للشيء، ومحل ذلك الشيء، وشرطه وسببه، فالعين الصلاة، والركن القيام والقراءة وغيرها، والمحل: هو الآدمي المكلف والشرط ما تقدم من الطهارة ،وغيرها والحكم جواز الصلاة وفسادها وثوابها، والسبب: الأوقات، والصفة ههنا بمعنى الكيفية المشتملة على فرض وواجب وسنة ومندوب لاشتمال الباب على الكل. (فتح) فرضها التحريمة [الأول] هو ما ثبت لزومه بدليل قطعي، فهو شامل للشرط والركن، والتحريم: جعل الشيء محرما، وزيادة التاء فيه للنقل من الوصفية إلى الاسمية وللوحدة والمبالغة وخصت التكبيرة الأولى؛ لأنها تحرم الأشياء المباحة المنافية للصلاة، والدليل على فرضيتها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِرْ﴾ (المدثر:٣) مع ما واظب عليه النبي (فتح) والقيام والثاني القيام ركن في الفرض دون النفل، وهو بحيث لو مد يديه لا ينال وركبتيه. (ع)] لقوله تعالى: وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ ﴾ (البقرة:۲۳۸) أي مطيعين أو ساكتين، والمراد به قيام الصلاة لإجماع المفسرين، والمفروض فيه بقدر القراءة، والأقرب للخشوع أن يكون بين قدميه أربع أصابع اليد والأولى في القيام أن يكون القدمان على الأرض، فلو قام على عقبيه أو أطراف أصابعه، أو رافعاً إحدى رجليه يجزئه، ويكره إن كان بغير عذر. (فتح) والقراءة [ والثالث: القراءة مطلقاً . من غير خصوصية الفاتحة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَلُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ﴾ (المزمل:۲۰) ولقوله : "ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن، وعلى فرضيتها انعقد الإجماع. الركوع والرابع: الركوع وهو انحناء الظهر إذا ركع قائما، فإن ركع جالساً فينبغي أن تحاذى جبهته قدام ركبتيه ليحصل الركوع والركن فيه أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم الركوع، وما زاد عليه واجب أو مستحب. السجود: [والخامس: السجود؛ لقوله تعالى : وارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا (الحج: ۷۷) وهو بجبهته وقدميه، ووضع أصبع واحدة شرط.] المراد جنسه، فإن الغرض تعداد الفرائض، ولهذا ذكر القيام والركوع مفرداً، والسجود: وضع بعض الوجه على الأرض مما لا سخرية فيه، فدخل الأنف وخرج الخد والذقن والصدغ. (فتح)
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Its fard [components] are: the takbirat al-ihram, standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. That is, the fards of prayer are seven. Chapter on the Description of Prayer: i.e., regarding clarifying its description. And 'description' (sifa) is the necessary sign of a thing. 'Description of prayer': A beginning on the conditioned [prayer] after explaining the condition. The idafa [construct phrase] is like adding a part to the whole. The intention is to clarify prayer and uncover its reality; thus the idafa is for the loosest relation. And 'sifa' and 'wasf' are verbal nouns like wa'd and 'idda. Know that for the establishment of something, six things are necessary: the essence ('ayn), which is the reality of the thing; the pillar (rukn), which is part of the reality; the ruling (hukm), which is the affirmation of the effect established for the thing; the locus of that thing; its condition; and its cause. So the essence is prayer; the pillars are standing, recitation, etc.; the locus is the legally responsible human; the condition is what preceded of purification, etc.; the ruling is the permissibility, invalidity, and reward of prayer; and the cause is the times. And 'sifa' here means 'quality' (kayfiyya), which includes fard, wajib, sunnah, and mandub, because the chapter encompasses all. (Fath) 'Its fard: the takbirat al-ihram' [First:] It is what is established as necessary by a definitive proof, so it includes both condition and pillar. 'Tahrima' means making something forbidden; the addition of the 'ta' is for the transfer from adjectival to nominal, for singularity, and for intensity. It is specifically applied to the first takbir because it prohibits permissible things that are incompatible with prayer. The proof for its being fard is His statement: 'And your Lord glorify' (al-Muddaththir: 3), along with the Prophet's continuous practice. (Fath) 'And standing': The second: Standing is a pillar in the fard prayer but not in the supererogatory. It is such that if he extends his hands he cannot reach his knees. (Ayni) Because of His statement: 'And stand before Allah with devotion' (al-Baqarah: 238), meaning obedient or silent. And what is meant is standing in prayer, by consensus of the commentators. The obligatory amount is the extent of recitation. What is closest to humility is that there be four finger-lengths between his feet. It is preferable for the feet to be on the ground. If he stands on his heels, the tips of his toes, or raises one foot, it suffices, but it is disliked (makruh) if without excuse. (Fath) 'And recitation': The third: Recitation absolutely, not specific to al-Fatiha, because of His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' (al-Muzzammil: 20), and his statement: 'Then recite what is easy from the Qur'an.' And consensus has been formed on its being fard. 'The bowing': The fourth: Bowing. It is the bending of the back when bowing while standing. If he bows while sitting, his forehead should be in line with the front of his knees for the bowing to be realized. The pillar in it is the minimum that is called bowing; any addition is wajib or mustahabb. 'The prostration': The fifth: Prostration, because of His statement: 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Hajj: 77). It is with his forehead and feet; placing one finger is a condition. What is meant is its genus, because the purpose is the enumeration of the fards; therefore standing and bowing are mentioned individually. Prostration is placing part of the face on the ground without something of mockery; thus the nose is included, and the cheek, chin, and temple are excluded. (Fath)
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on the description of prayer (sifa). It lists five fard (obligatory) components: takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir), standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). The commentary clarifies that 'description' here means the quality (kayfiyya) that encompasses fard, wajib, sunnah, and mandub. The author first provides a theoretical framework for understanding the components of any act: essence, pillar, ruling, locus, condition, and cause. Applying this to prayer, the essence is prayer itself; the pillars include standing and recitation; the locus is the responsible Muslim; conditions include purification; the ruling covers validity, invalidity, and reward; and the cause is the times. The commentary then explains each fard. For takbirat al-ihram, it is fard based on the command in Surah al-Muddaththir (74:3) and the Prophet's continuous practice. The term 'tahrima' is specific to this takbir because it prohibits those permissible acts that conflict with prayer. For standing (qiyam), it is a pillar in fard prayers but not in nafl; its requirement is supported by Surah al-Baqarah (2:238). The obligatory extent of standing is the duration of recitation. Standing on heels or toes is valid but disliked if without excuse. For recitation, any portion of the Qur'an suffices, based on Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20) and the hadith 'then recite what is easy from the Qur'an.' Consensus confirms its obligation. For bowing, the minimum bending is sufficient; the commentary specifies the proper form if bowing while seated. For prostration, it is fard based on Surah al-Hajj (22:77). It is performed with the forehead and feet; placing even one finger on the ground is a condition. The 'prostration' referred to is the genus, i.e., the act itself. The face placed must be some part without mockery, so the nose is included but the cheek, chin, and temple are not sufficient. Note: The text says 'the fards of prayer are seven' but only five are enumerated here; the remaining two (perhaps the final sitting and something else) are discussed later in the chapter.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
ركن (rukn): A pillar of the prayer, i.e., an integral part without which the prayer is invalid.
فرض (fard): In this context, fard is synonymous with rukn; an obligatory component established by definitive proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Recitation of al-Fatiha specifically
C) Standing (qiyam)
D) Bowing (ruku)

Key Takeaway
The five fards of prayer are the essential pillars that must be present for the prayer to be valid; each is proven by a direct Quranic command.

The First Five Fards of Prayer: Takbir, Qiyam, Qira'ah, Ruku', Sujud
Listing and proving the first five fards of prayer with textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first five fards of prayer, explain their proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and identify the minimum requirement for each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The five fards from takbir to sujud are proven by explicit Quranic commands and Prophetic practice, with the Hanafi school defining the minimum for each.

This lesson covers the first five of the seven fards of prayer: the opening takbir, standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary provides the Quranic and hadith evidence for each, along with the Hanafi school's interpretation of the minimum that fulfills the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first fard: Takbir al-Ihram
Read the passage to understand that the opening takbir is the first fard. Note the proof from the Quran (74:3) and the Prophet's continuous practice.
The term 'tahrimah' indicates that this takbir makes worldly affairs forbidden during prayer.
2
Analyze the second fard: Standing (Qiyam)
Standing is a pillar for fard prayers. The proof is Quran 2:238. The minimum is the ability to stand straight enough to recite. Note the conditions for valid standing.
Standing on heels or toes is sufficient but disliked without excuse.
3
Examine the third fard: Recitation (Qira'ah)
Recitation of any portion of the Quran is fard, not specifically al-Fatihah. Proof: Quran 73:20 and the hadith 'then recite what is easy of the Quran.' Consensus supports its fardiyyah.
The Hanafi school holds that any Quranic verses suffice, unlike the Shafi'i who require al-Fatihah.
4
Understand the fourth fard: Bowing (Ruku')
Bowing is proven by Quran 22:77 alongside prostration. The minimum is the least that can be called bowing (bending the back).
If one bows while sitting, the forehead should be in front of the knees.
5
Explore the fifth fard: Prostration (Sujud)
Prostration is proven by the same verse. It requires placing part of the face (forehead and nose) on the ground, along with the feet. Placing one finger is a condition.
The minimum contact is the forehead; the nose is included. Cheeks, chin, etc. are excluded.
