(ع)] لقوله علي لابن مسعود حين علمه التشهد: "إذا قلت هذا أو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك أي وأنت قاعد للإجماع على أن قراءة التشهد في غير القعود لا تعتبر، علق الإتمام بالفعل قرأ التشهد أو لم يقرأ ولا يرد عليه أنه عليها علق الإتمام بأحدهما، وهو القعدة أو القعود مع القراءة، والقراءة فرض؛ لأن هذا يخالف الإجماع؛ إذ لم يقل أحد بفرضية قراءة التشهد، فإن قيل: كيف ثبتت الفرضية بخبر الواحد؟ قلنا: هذا الخبر وقع بياناً لمجمل الكتاب وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ﴾ (البقرة:٤٣)، فكان ثبوت الفرضية بالكتاب لا به كما في خبر المسح على الرأس. (مستخلص) والخروج بصنعه: [ أي والسابع خروج المصلي من صلاته. (ع)][ أي بفعله المنافي للصلاة وإن كره تحريماً، والصحيح: أنه ليس بفرض اتفاقاً بل واجب. (ع)] أي بفعله مطلقاً، سواء كان بلفظ السلام أو غيره، وعند الشافعي: بلفظ السلام فقط؛ لقوله عليه : " وتحليلها التسليم، ولنا ما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود ، وما رواه لا يدل على الفرضية؛ لكونه خبرا واحدا ، بل على الواجب، وقد قلنا به وعندهما الخروج بصنعه ليس بفرض. (فتح)
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Its fard are: the saying of Allahu Akbar to commence prayer, standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration — meaning the fard of prayer are seven. Chapter on the Description of Prayer: that is, in explaining its description. And as-sifah (description) is the necessary mark of a thing. Description of prayer: beginning the conditioned after the condition has been explained, and the idafah (construct phrase) here is like adding a part to the whole. The intent is to clarify prayer and reveal its essence, so the idafah is for the slightest connection. As-sifah and al-wasf are two verbal nouns like al-wa'd and al-'iddah. Know that for the establishment of a thing six things are necessary: the essence which is the quiddity of the thing, the pillar which is a part of the essence, the ruling which is the affirmation of the effect established for the thing, the locus of that thing, its condition, and its cause. So the essence is prayer, the pillar is standing, recitation, etc., the locus is the legally responsible human being, the condition is what preceded of purification etc., the ruling is the permissibility of prayer, its invalidity, and its reward, the cause is the times. And as-sifah here is in the sense of the modality that includes fard, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb, because the chapter includes all. (Fath) Its fard: [First] Takbir al-Ihram — it is what is established as binding by a definitive proof, so it includes both condition and pillar. Tahrim: making a thing forbidden; the extra ta' is for transfer from adjective to noun, and for singularity and exaggeration. It is specifically the first takbir because it forbids permissible things contradictory to prayer. The proof of its being fard is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3) along with the Prophet's constant practice. (Fath) And standing: [Second] Standing is a pillar in fard prayer, not in supererogatory prayer. It is such that if he stretched his hands he would not reach his knees. (Ayni) Because of His saying: 'And stand before Allah devoutly obedient' (2:238) meaning obedient or silent. What is intended by it is the standing of prayer by consensus of the exegetes. What is obligatory in it is to the extent of recitation. Closest to humility is that there be four fingers of the hand between his feet. The better in standing is that both feet be on the ground. If he stood on his heels or on the tips of his toes, or lifting one of his feet, it suffices him, but it is disliked if without excuse. (Fath) And recitation: [Third] Recitation absolutely, without specification of al-Fatihah, because of His saying: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20) and his saying: 'Then recite what is easy of the Quran with you.' And consensus has been reached on its being fard. Bowing: [Fourth] Bowing is bending the back when bowing while standing. If he bows while sitting, then his forehead should be in front of his knees in order to achieve bowing. The pillar in it is the least that the name 'bowing' applies to. What exceeds that is wajib or mustahabb. Prostration: [Fifth] Prostration, because of His saying: 'Bow and prostrate' (22:77). It is with his forehead and feet. Placing one finger is a condition. What is meant is its genus, for the purpose is to enumerate the faraid. Therefore standing and bowing are mentioned in singular. Prostration is placing part of the face on the ground that does not involve mockery. So the nose is included, and the cheek, chin, and temple are excluded. (Fath) And the final sitting: [Sixth] The sitting posture is a fard but not a pillar. (Ayni) Because of his saying to Ibn Mas'ud when teaching him the tashahhud: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete' meaning while you are sitting, because of consensus that recitation of tashahhud in other than sitting is not considered. He linked completion to the act whether he recited the tashahhud or not. It is not objected against him that completion is linked to one of two things, which are sitting or sitting with recitation, and recitation is fard; because this contradicts consensus since no one has said that recitation of tashahhud is fard. If it is said: How is fardiyyah established by a solitary hadith? We say: This hadith occurred as an explanation of the abridged text of the Book, namely His saying: 'And establish prayer' (2:43). So the establishment of fardiyyah was by the Book, not by it, as in the report on wiping over the head. (Mukhtalaf) And exiting by his own action: [Seventh] The exit of the worshiper from his prayer. (Ayni) That is, by his action contradictory to prayer, even if it is prohibitively disliked. The correct view is that it is not fard by agreement, but wajib. (Ayni) That is, by his action absolutely, whether by the word of salam or other than it. According to al-Shafi'i, it is only by the word of salam because of his saying: 'Its tahrimah (opening) is the takbir and its tahlilah (closing) is the taslim.' Our proof is what we have narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. And what he narrated does not indicate fardiyyah because it is a single hadith, but rather indicates wujoob (obligation). We have said that. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), exiting by his own action is not fard. (Fath)
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the seven fard (obligatory pillars) of prayer in the Hanafi school. It begins by defining the chapter heading and then distinguishes between essence, pillar, ruling, locus, condition, and cause. The author then lists each fard: (1) Takbir al-Ihram (the opening takbir), proven by the Quranic command to magnify Allah and the Prophet's continuous practice. (2) Qiyam (standing), required in fard prayer, with the amount being the duration of recitation; standing on heels or toes is permissible but disliked. (3) Qira'ah (recitation), which is absolute and not specific to Surah al-Fatihah, based on the verse 'Recite what is easy of the Quran' and the hadith of the teaching of prayer. (4) Ruku' (bowing), defined as bending the back; the minimum constitutes the pillar. (5) Sujud (prostration), proven by the command 'Bow and prostrate'; it must be with the forehead and feet. (6) Al-Qu'ud al-Akhir (final sitting), which is a fard but not a pillar (rukn) according to Hanafis; it is established by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the prayer is complete when one sits and says the tashahhud. (7) Al-Khuruj bi-Sun'ihi (exiting by one's own action), which according to the relied-upon position is wajib, not fard, and includes any intentional action that ends the prayer, whether by salam or otherwise. The text also includes a discussion with al-Shafi'i regarding the exit: the Shafi'i school requires only the salam, while the Hanafi school maintains that any deliberate exiting action suffices. The commentary clarifies that the final sitting and exiting are not universally agreed upon as fard; some authorities consider them wajib.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that makes the prayer forbidden for worldly affairs.
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing posture during prayer, specifically in fard prayers.
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of any portion of the Quran during prayer.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing the back during prayer.
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration: placing part of the face (forehead and nose) on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum required for recitation (qira'ah) in prayer?
A) Recitation of Surah al-Fatihah only
B) Recitation of any three short verses
C) Recitation of any portion of the Quran, even one verse
D) Recitation must be in Arabic and at least one verse

Key Takeaway
The first five fards of prayer (takbir, standing, recitation, bowing, prostration) are each established by clear Quranic commands, with the Hanafi school defining the minimum for each.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Final Sitting and Exiting Prayer: Fard, Wajib, or Both?
Explaining the final sitting and exiting, with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the final sitting is fard but not a rukn in the Hanafi school, contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on exiting prayer, and apply the ruling to a scenario of exiting without salam.

Core Idea
The final sitting is a fard but not a pillar; exiting the prayer is wajib, not fard, and can be by any forbidden action, not limited to salam.

This lesson focuses on the sixth and seventh fards according to the Hanafi list: the final sitting (al-qu'ud al-akhir) and exiting the prayer (al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi). The text explains that the final sitting is fard but not a rukn, while exiting is wajib by agreement, and then presents the dispute with al-Shafi'i on whether the exit is specifically by salam or by any deliberate action.

Guided Path
1
Understand the status of the final sitting
Read the passage that says the final sitting is fard but not a rukn (pillar). Note that this is a unique Hanafi position: it is an obligatory element that must be performed, but its omission does not invalidate the prayer in the same way as a missing rukn; rather, the prayer becomes invalid because it is fard.
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete.' This ties completion to the sitting act.
2
Analyze the proof for the final sitting
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is a khabar wahid (solitary hadith). The Hanafi school uses it as a bayan (explanation) of the general command to establish prayer (Quran 2:43). Therefore, the fardiyyah is established by the Quran, not the hadith alone. This usul point is crucial.
The similar example is the wiping over the head in wudu: the Quran commands wiping, and the Sunnah explains the extent.
3
Examine the ruling on exiting (khuruj)
The text states that exiting the prayer is wajib, not fard, by agreement. The 'correct view' is that it is wajib. This means that if a person exits without salam, the prayer ends (it is valid) but he has sinned by violating a wajib.
The Shafi'i school holds that exiting is only by the word of salam (taslim) and it is fard, not wajib.
4
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i proofs
Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'Its tahrimah is the takbir and its tahlilah is the taslim.' Hanafi responds that this hadith is khabar wahid and thus indicates wujoob, not fardiyyah. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which shows that the prayer is complete by the sitting, not by a specific exit formula.
The Hanafi school also notes that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that exiting by one's own action is not fard (i.e., it is only wajib).
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who, after the final sitting, gets up and walks away without saying salam. In the Hanafi school, his prayer is valid (since the fard of sitting was fulfilled) but he is sinning for abandoning the wajib of exiting properly (which is preferably by salam).
According to Shafi'i, the prayer would be invalid because the exit was not by salam.

باب صفة الصلاة
فرضها التحريمة والقيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود أي فرض الصلاة سبعة
باب صفة الصلاة: أي في بيان صفتها والصفة: الإمارة اللازمة للشيء. صفة الصلاة : شروع في المشروط بعد بيان الشرط والإضافة فيه كإضافة الجزء إلى الكل، والمراد تبيين الصلاة وكشف ماهيتها، فالإضافة لأدنى ملابسة والصفة والوصف مصدران كالوعد والعدة. واعلم أنه يشترط لثبوت الشيء ستة أشياء: العين وهي ماهية الشيء، والركن وهو جزء الماهية، والحكم وهو إثبات الأثر الثابت للشيء، ومحل ذلك الشيء، وشرطه وسببه، فالعين الصلاة، والركن القيام والقراءة وغيرها، والمحل: هو الآدمي المكلف والشرط ما تقدم من الطهارة ،وغيرها والحكم جواز الصلاة وفسادها وثوابها، والسبب: الأوقات،
والصفة ههنا بمعنى الكيفية المشتملة على فرض وواجب وسنة ومندوب لاشتمال الباب على الكل. (فتح) فرضها التحريمة [الأول] هو ما ثبت لزومه بدليل قطعي، فهو شامل للشرط والركن، والتحريم: جعل الشيء محرما، وزيادة التاء فيه للنقل من الوصفية إلى الاسمية وللوحدة والمبالغة وخصت التكبيرة الأولى؛ لأنها تحرم الأشياء المباحة المنافية للصلاة، والدليل على فرضيتها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبَرْ﴾ (المدثر:٣) مع ما واظب عليه
النبي (فتح)

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the seven fard (obligatory pillars) of prayer in the Hanafi school. It begins by defining the chapter heading and then distinguishes between essence, pillar, ruling, locus, condition, and cause. The author then lists each fard: (1) Takbir al-Ihram (the opening takbir), proven by the Quranic command to magnify Allah and the Prophet's continuous practice. (2) Qiyam (standing), required in fard prayer, with the amount being the duration of recitation; standing on heels or toes is permissible but disliked. (3) Qira'ah (recitation), which is absolute and not specific to Surah al-Fatihah, based on the verse 'Recite what is easy of the Quran' and the hadith of the teaching of prayer. (4) Ruku' (bowing), defined as bending the back; the minimum constitutes the pillar. (5) Sujud (prostration), proven by the command 'Bow and prostrate'; it must be with the forehead and feet. (6) Al-Qu'ud al-Akhir (final sitting), which is a fard but not a pillar (rukn) according to Hanafis; it is established by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the prayer is complete when one sits and says the tashahhud. (7) Al-Khuruj bi-Sun'ihi (exiting by one's own action), which according to the relied-upon position is wajib, not fard, and includes any intentional action that ends the prayer, whether by salam or otherwise. The text also includes a discussion with al-Shafi'i regarding the exit: the Shafi'i school requires only the salam, while the Hanafi school maintains that any deliberate exiting action suffices. The commentary clarifies that the final sitting and exiting are not universally agreed upon as fard; some authorities consider them wajib.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The sitting posture in the final rak'ah for the duration of reciting the tashahhud.
الخروج بصنعه (al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi): Exiting the prayer by one's own deliberate action that is incompatible with the prayer state.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that makes the prayer forbidden for worldly affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of the final sitting (al-qu'ud al-akhir) in prayer?
A) It is a rukn (pillar) of prayer
B) It is a fard but not a rukn
C) It is a wajib that requires sujud al-sahw if omitted
D) It is a sunnah

Key Takeaway
The final sitting is fard but not a rukn, and exiting the prayer is wajib, with the Hanafi school allowing any deliberate action to end the prayer.

The Wajib Acts of Prayer: Reciting al-Fatihah and Adding a Surah
Defining two wajib acts and debating their fard/wajib status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah in prayer, explain why they are wajib not fard, and evaluate the inter-school debate on this issue.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib, not fard: the qat'i obligation is any Quran recitation; the specific choice is from zanni dalil.

This lesson examines two wajib acts of prayer: reciting Surah al-Fatihah and adding another surah (or equivalent verses). In the Hanafi school, these are distinct from the fard (pillar) of qira'ah (any Quran recitation). We will explore the evidence, the difference between fard and wajib, and the inter-school debate that hinges on how we interpret certain hadith.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish fard and wajib in Hanafi usul
Understand that fard is established by definitive proof (qat'i) and its rejection leads to disbelief, while wajib is from conjectural proof (zanni) and rejection does not cause disbelief, though both are binding in practice.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the two wajib acts in prayer
The text states that reciting all of al-Fatihah and adding a surah (or three short verses or one long verse) are wajib. Recognize that these are additional specifications beyond the fard of absolute recitation.
The second wajib applies in the first two rak'ah of fard prayer and all rak'ah of nafl prayer.
3
Review the opposing view that Fatihah is fard
Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and in one narration Imam Muhammad hold that reciting al-Fatihah is fard (pillar). Their evidence includes the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatihah of the Book' and 'Whoever prays without Umm al-Quran, it is deficient.'
This is a key point of inter-school ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proofs from Quran and hadith
The Hanafi response cites Quran 73:20 ('Recite what is easy of the Quran') and the Bedouin hadith where the Prophet taught general recitation without specifying Fatihah. They argue the opposing hadith are interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity.
The Bedouin hadith is used to show that if Fatihah were fard, the Prophet would have specifically taught it.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah) between the views
For Hanafis, if a worshiper recites another surah instead of al-Fatihah, the prayer is valid but deficient (requires sajdah al-sahw). For Shafi'is, such a prayer would be invalid. This difference stems directly from the ruling on the obligation level.
This illustrates the real-world impact of usul distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وواجبها هو ما ثبت لزومه بدليل ظني، وهو والفرض في العمل سواء، والفرق في الاعتقاد، فمنكر الفرض القطعي كافر، بخلاف الواجب، أما لو ترك ما وجب في الصلاة سهواً يجب عليه سجدته، وأما عمداً وإن لم يكن مبطلاً للصلاة لكن يوجب الإعادة (عيني، فتح) قراءة الفاتحة أي كلها واجبة فيسجد بترك آية منها، وتعاد وجوبا في العمد والسهو وإن لم يسجد له ولم يعدها يكون آئماً فاسقاً، وعند مالك والشافعي وعند محمد في رواية: فرض؛ لقوله علي: "لا" صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب"، وقوله: "من صلى صلاة لم يقرأ فيها بأم القرآن فهي خداج"، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ ﴾ (المزمل: ٢٠)، والزيادة عليه بخبر الواحد لا تجوز، لكنه يوجب العمل، وقد قلنا به، ومعنى الحديث الأول : لا صلاة كاملة الثواب بدليل قوله علي للأعرابي: "إذا قمت إلى الصلاة فأسبغ الوضوء، ثم استقبل القبلة فكبر، ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن"، فلو كان فرضاً لعلّمه إياها؛ لجهله بالأحكام وحاجته إليها، ولا دلالة في الحديث الثاني؛ لأن الخداج: النقصان، فلا يدل على عدم الجواز بل على النقص، ونحن نقول به، وأيضا الحديث الأول ليس بمحكم بل محتمل لأن يراد به نفي الجواز ونفي الكمال، فتعين الحمل على نفي الكمال بدليل حديث آخر، فلا تجوز به الزيادة ولو كان مشهوراً؛ لأنه ليس محكم. (فتح) وضم سورة [ أي مع الفاتحة أو ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة بقدرها وهو الواجب الثاني. (ع ، ط واعلم أن ضم السورة وإن لم يكن فرضاً بعد ما قرأ الفاتحة لكنه إذا ضمها الفاتحة مع تقع عن الفرض والحاصل أن مطلق القراءة ،فرض وخصوصية كونها فاتحة وسورة واجبة وفي ضمن أداء الواجبين يؤدى الفرض كذا في بعض الشروح.
And its wajib (obligatory) acts are what is established as binding by a conjectural proof (dalil zanni). It and the fard are the same in practice, the difference lies in belief. Thus, one who denies a qat'i (definitive) fard is a disbeliever, unlike the wajib. As for if one leaves what is wajib in prayer unintentionally, he must perform a prostration (sajdah) for it. If intentionally, even if it does not invalidate the prayer, it necessitates repetition. (Ayni, Fath) Recitation of al-Fatihah: i.e., all of it is wajib, so one prostrates for leaving a verse of it. It must be repeated wajiban (obligatorily) in both intentional and unintentional omission, even if he did not prostrate for it and did not repeat it, he becomes sinful and corrupt. According to Malik, al-Shafi'i, and according to Muhammad in one narration, it is fard, because of his saying: 'No prayer (is valid) except with the Fatihah of the Book', and his saying: 'Whoever prays a prayer in which he does not recite Umm al-Quran, it is deficient (khidaj)'. Our proof is the saying of Allah: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20). And adding (to the text) by a single narration is not allowed, but it necessitates action, and we have said that. The meaning of the first hadith is 'no prayer has complete reward', as evidenced by his saying to the Bedouin: 'When you stand for prayer, perform wudu properly, then face the qiblah, then say takbir, then recite what is easy of the Quran with you.' If it were fard, he would have taught it to him, because he was ignorant of the rulings and in need of it. And there is no indication in the second hadith because khidaj means deficiency, so it does not indicate impermissibility but deficiency. And we adhere to that. Also, the first hadith is not decisive (muhkam) but is susceptible to meaning negation of permissibility or negation of perfection. So it is necessarily interpreted as negation of perfection by evidence of another hadith. Therefore, an addition (to the Quran) by a famous hadith is not allowed because it is not decisive. (Fath) And adding a surah: i.e., with al-Fatihah, or three short verses (ayat) or one long verse of equivalent length. This is the second wajib. (Ayni, Tawdih) Know that the addition of a surah, even though it is not fard after having recited al-Fatihah, when he adds it, the Fatihah performs the duty. The gist is that absolute recitation is fard, and the specification that it be al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib. In the performance of the two wajib, the fard is performed. This is as stated in some commentaries.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage explains the two wajib (obligatory but not fard) acts of prayer in the Hanafi school: reciting Surah al-Fatihah and reciting another surah (or equivalent verses) after it. The text first defines the difference between fard and wajib: both are binding in practice, but fard is established by definitive proof (qat'i) while wajib is from conjectural proof (zanni). Denial of fard leads to disbelief, while denial of wajib does not. If a wajib is left unintentionally, one performs sajdah al-sahw; if left intentionally, the prayer is still valid but must be repeated (this is emphasized for Fatihah specifically). The text then engages in an inter-school dispute: Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and in one narration Imam Muhammad consider reciting Fatihah as fard, citing the hadith 'No prayer except with Fatihah' and 'It is deficient'. The Hanafi response argues that the verse 'Recite what is easy of the Quran' supports absolute recitation, and the hadith about Fatihah is interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity. The Bedouin hadith shows the Prophet taught only to recite what is easy, not specifically Fatihah. Thus, Fatihah is not fard but wajib. The passage concludes that the second wajib is adding a surah (or three short verses/one long verse) after Fatihah. The overall structure: the fard is the act of reciting any Quran (muttlak al-qira'ah), and the specific obligation of Fatihah and surah is at the level of wajib.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligation established by a conjectural proof (dalil zanni). It is binding in practice but denial does not lead to disbelief.
الفاتحة (al-fatiha): The first surah of the Quran, consisting of seven verses, which must be recited in every rak'ah of prayer as a wajib act.
ضم سورة (damm surah): To add a complete surah or three verses (or equivalent) after reciting al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ah of fard prayer, or in all rak'ah of supererogatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet explicitly said it is fard only for the imam
B) Because the proof is a solitary hadith (khabar wahid), which is zanni, and the Quranic verse allows any recitation
C) Because al-Fatihah is not part of the Quran
D) Because it was abrogated in the later years of Islam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah are wajib (conjectural obligations), not fard; the essential obligation is any Quran recitation.

The Final Sitting: Fard but Not a Rukn
Ruling that the final sitting is fard (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar), with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the final sitting and explain why it is considered fard rather than a rukn, using the proof from the hadith and the argument from bayan al-mujmal.

Core Idea
The final sitting is fard, not a rukn: its omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the prayer.

In the Hanafi school, the final sitting (al-qu'ūd al-ākhir) after the last prostration is a distinct obligation. Unlike a rukn (pillar), whose omission makes the prayer invalid, the sitting is a fard that can be compensated through sajdah sahw. The proof comes from a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught the tashahhud to Ibn Mas'ud, saying 'when you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' This hadith, though a khabar wahid, explains the general Quranic command to establish prayer, thus establishing the obligation through the Quran itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the final sitting is a fard (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar). Note that this is a specific category within prayer: it is essential but not an integral whose omission invalidates.
The text uses 'فَرْضٌ لَيْسَ بِرُكْنٍ' – fard not rukn.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' The phrase 'or do this' refers to the sitting itself. The commenter argues that completion is attached to the action (sitting) irrespective of recitation.
The hadith is a khabar wahid, transmitted through one chain.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'أَوْ' (or) indicates that sitting alone suffices for completion. Therefore the sitting is an obligatory part. The recitation of tashahhud, though mentioned, is not fard by consensus.
The phrase 'أسأل الله الجنة' in the hadith shows the 'do this' refers to the sitting.
4
Address the objection about khabar wahid
How can a khabar wahid establish fardiyyah? The answer: this hadith is a bayan (explanation) of the mujmal (general) command in the Quran, 'And establish prayer' (2:43). The obligation ultimately derives from the Quran, not the hadith alone, similar to the ruling of wiping over the head.
Thus the proof is considered qat'i in terms of obligation, even though the hadith itself is zanni al-thubut.
5
Distinguish from a rukn and note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
A rukn invalidates the prayer if omitted. The final sitting is fard only; its omission is compensated by sajdah sahw. Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider it a rukn, but the Hanafi position is that it is not.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): if the sitting is forgotten, Hanafis require sajdah sahw; Shafi'is consider the prayer invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقعود الأخير: [والسادس: القعدة وهو فرض ليس بركن. (ع)] لقوله علي لابن مسعود حين علمه التشهد: "إذا قلت هذا أو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك أي وأنت قاعد للإجماع على أن قراءة التشهد في غير القعود لا تعتبر، علق الإتمام بالفعل قرأ التشهد أو لم يقرأ ولا يرد عليه أنه عليها علق الإتمام بأحدهما، وهو القعدة أو القعود مع القراءة، والقراءة فرض؛ لأن هذا يخالف الإجماع؛ إذ لم يقل أحد بفرضية قراءة التشهد، فإن قيل: كيف ثبتت الفرضية بخبر الواحد؟ قلنا: هذا الخبر وقع بياناً لمجمل الكتاب وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ﴾ (البقرة:٤٣)، فكان ثبوت الفرضية بالكتاب لا به كما في خبر المسح على الرأس. (مستخلص)
And the final sitting: [The sixth is the sitting, and it is a fard (obligation) not a rukn (pillar).] Due to his statement (Ali) to Ibn Mas'ud when he taught him the tashahhud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete' meaning while you are sitting. Because of the consensus that recitation of tashahhud in other than the sitting is not considered. He attached completion to the action, whether he recited tashahhud or not. And it is not objected that he attached completion to one of two things, which is the sitting or the sitting with recitation, and recitation is fard; because this opposes consensus; since no one has said the recitation of tashahhud is fard. If it is said: How is fardiyyah established by a khabar wahid? We say: This khabar occurred as an explanation of the mujmal of the Book, which is His saying: 'And establish prayer' (2:43). So the establishment of fardiyyah is by the Book, not by it (the hadith), as in the hadith of wiping over the head. (Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the legal status of the final sitting (al-qu'ūd al-ākhir) in prayer. The commentator explains that, according to the Hanafi school, the final sitting is a fard (obligatory act) but not a rukn (pillar). The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught the tashahhud and said when you say/do this, your prayer is complete. The phrase 'or do this' refers to the sitting itself, and completion is attached to the sitting regardless of recitation. This shows the sitting is obligatory. However, recitation of tashahhud is not fard by consensus. An objection arises: how can fardiyyah be established by a single-transmission hadith? The answer: the hadith explains the general command in the Quran to establish prayer, so the obligation is ultimately from the Quran, not the hadith alone, similar to the ruling of wiping over the head.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ūd al-ākhir): The final sitting in prayer, after the last prostration, before exiting.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act whose obligation is proven by definitive evidence; denial is kufr.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāhid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is a fard (obligatory) but not a rukn.
C) It is a sunnah (recommended).
D) It is mustahab (preferable).

Key Takeaway
The final sitting in prayer is a fard (obligatory) but not a rukn; it is established by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud which explains the general command to pray.

Exiting Prayer: Wajib by Any Nullifying Act
Ruling that exiting prayer is wajib and done by any intentional act, not only salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exiting prayer, explain why it is wajib rather than fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Exiting prayer is wajib and achieved by any intentional nullifying act, not only by salam.

When a person wants to leave the state of prayer, what counts as a valid exit? The Hanafi school holds that any deliberate action that nullifies the prayer—such as speaking, eating, or breaking wudu—accomplishes the exit, though it is discouraged to do so without salam. This lesson examines the ruling, the proof, and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that 'exiting by one's action' (al-khurūj bi-ṣun'ih) is the subject. The Hanafi ruling: it is wajib, not fard, and achieved by any action that nullifies prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (reported by Abu Hanifa). The Shafi'i proof is the hadith 'And its tahlil is the salam'.
Both are ahad hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi use of Ibn Mas'ud's hadith implies that exiting can occur by any nullifying act, not only salam. The Shafi'i use of the other hadith claims exclusivity. The Hanafis respond that the Shafi'i hadith is khabar wahid and indicates wujub, not fard.
The difference between fard (certain) and wajib (probable) is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'i holds that exiting is only by salam and is fard. Hanafis say it is wajib and by any nullifying act. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also hold it is not fard.
Thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in validity and repetition.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. Exiting by other than salam is makruh tahriman but valid. The salam remains the sunnah method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخروج بصنعه: [ أي والسابع خروج المصلي من صلاته. (ع)][ أي بفعله المنافي للصلاة وإن كره تحريماً، والصحيح: أنه ليس بفرض اتفاقاً بل واجب. (ع)] أي بفعله مطلقاً، سواء كان بلفظ السلام أو غيره، وعند الشافعي: بلفظ السلام فقط؛ لقوله عليه : " وتحليلها التسليم، ولنا ما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود ، وما رواه لا يدل على الفرضية؛ لكونه خبرا واحدا ، بل على الواجب، وقد قلنا به وعندهما الخروج بصنعه ليس بفرض. (فتح)
And exiting by his action: [i.e. the seventh is the exiting of the prayer from his prayer. (al-'Inaya)] [i.e. by his action that nullifies the prayer, even if it is tahriman makruh. And the correct view: it is not fard by agreement but rather wajib. (al-'Inaya)] i.e. by his action absolutely, whether by the word of salam or other than it. And according to al-Shafi'i: by the word of salam only, because of his statement: 'And its tahlil is the salam.' And we have what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. And what he narrated does not indicate fardiyyah because it is a khabar wahid, but rather indicates obligation (wujub), and we have said it. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), exiting by one's action is not fard. (Fath)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage discusses the seventh obligation of prayer: exiting (al-khurūj). The Hanafi position, as maintained by Abu Hanifa, is that exiting prayer is achieved by any deliberate act that nullifies the prayer (such as breaking wudu, speaking, etc.), not only by saying the salam. However, it is not fard but wajib by agreement. The Shafi'i school holds that exiting is only by the salam, based on the hadith: 'And its tahlil is the salam.' The Hanafi response: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud does not prove fardiyyah because it is a khabar wahid; rather it indicates wujub. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also say it is not fard.

Key Terms
الخروج بصنعه (al-khurūj bi-ṣun'ih): Exiting the prayer by one's own deliberate action that nullifies the prayer state.
تحليلها التسليم (taḥlīluhā al-taslīm): What makes prayer permissible (i.e., permissible to exit) is the salam.
خبر واحد (khabar wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few chains, which does not reach the level of certainty (tawatur).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Exiting the prayer is optional; one may stay in the prayer state indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that exiting prayer is wajib and validly achieved by any intentional act that nullifies the prayer, though the salam is the preferred method.

Distinction Between Fard and Wajib
Definition of wājib and its distinction from fard with practical consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wājib, distinguish it from fard in terms of evidence and belief, and apply the consequences of omitting a wajib in prayer.

Core Idea
Wajib is proven by speculative evidence; it binds in action like fard, but denial does not cause disbelief.

The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes fard from wājib, a distinction not made by other madhhabs. This passage from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq defines wājib as an obligation established by ẓannī (speculative) evidence. While both fard and wājib are equally binding in practice, the difference lies in the realm of belief: denying a fard can lead to kufr, whereas denying a wājib does not. The passage also outlines the consequences of omitting a wājib in prayer, whether forgetfully or intentionally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitional components
Look at what defines wājib: its evidential basis (ẓannī) and its relationship to fard.
The passage uses 'بدليل ظني' (by speculative evidence) and states equality in action.
2
Distinguish the legal consequences in action vs. belief
Both are equal in action, but differ in iʿtiqād. Denying fard is kufr; denying wājib is not.
The phrase 'والفرق في الاعتقاد' (the difference is in belief) is key.
3
Apply the ruling to omission scenarios
Forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw; intentional omission requires repetition (iʿāda).
The text says: 'سهواً يجب عليه سجدته' and 'عمداً يوجب الإعادة'.
4
Contrast with the Shāfiʿī position
Other schools equate fard and wājib, so for them omission of a 'wājib' (which they call fard) may invalidate the prayer.
This is a cross-madhhab difference noted in the hanafi_position_box.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وواجبها هو ما ثبت لزومه بدليل ظني، وهو والفرض في العمل سواء، والفرق في الاعتقاد، فمنكر الفرض القطعي كافر، بخلاف الواجب، أما لو ترك ما وجب في الصلاة سهواً يجب عليه سجدته، وأما عمداً وإن لم يكن مبطلاً للصلاة لكن يوجب الإعادة (عيني، فتح)
And its wajib is that whose necessity is established by speculative evidence, and it and the fard are equal in action, and the difference is in belief. So the denier of the decisive fard is a disbeliever, unlike the wajib. As for if one leaves what is wajib in prayer forgetfully, he must perform prostration for it. And as for intentionally, even if it does not invalidate the prayer, it necessitates repetition. (al-'Inayah, Fath)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of wājib within the Hanafi school. Wājib is an obligation proven by speculative (ẓannī) evidence, whereas fard is proven by definitive (qaṭ'ī) evidence. In terms of action, both are equally binding; one must perform them. The difference lies in i'tiqād (belief): denying a fard that is decisively proven constitutes disbelief, while denying a wājib does not reach that level. Regarding consequences in prayer: if a wājib is omitted forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw is required. If omitted intentionally, the prayer is not invalidated but must be repeated, and the person is sinful.

Key Terms
الفرض القطعي (al-farḍ al-qaṭ'ī): An obligation proven by definitive evidence (Qur'an, mutawatir Sunnah).
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligation proven by speculative evidence (khabar wahid, qiyas).
سجدته (sajdatihī): Prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) to compensate for an omitted wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of denying a fard (farḍ qaṭ'ī)?
A) It is a minor sin.
B) It requires prostration of forgetfulness.
C) It constitutes disbelief (kufr).
D) It has no consequence.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wājib is an obligation from speculative evidence, equal to fard in action but not in belief; its omission in prayer requires prostration if forgetful and repetition if intentional.

Recitation of Surah al-Fatihah: Wajib or Fard?
Ruling that reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, with proofs and dispute with other schools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds recitation of al-Fatihah as wajib and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard—omission requires compensation but does not invalidate prayer.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi school and other schools regarding the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in prayer. While the Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider it fard (obligatory) such that its omission invalidates the prayer, the Hanafi school holds it as wajib—still obligatory but with a lower evidentiary threshold. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school uses usul al-fiqh principles to weigh conflicting proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer and in all rak'ahs of nafl prayer is wajib, not fard.
Wajib means obligatory but established by zanni evidence; fard is established by qati evidence.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Muhammad (in one narration) hold that recitation of al-Fatihah is fard, i.e., a pillar whose omission invalidates the prayer.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Muhammad's other narration agrees with Abu Hanifa.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They cite two hadiths: 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' and 'Whoever prays without Umm al-Qur'an, it is deficient (khadaj).'
The term 'khadaj' is interpreted by opponents as meaning invalid.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond: The Quranic verse 73:20 commands reciting 'what is easy,' not specifically al-Fatihah. The hadiths indicate perfection, not validity. The hadith of the Bedouin shows the Prophet taught him to recite 'what is easy,' not al-Fatihah specifically. Also, the first hadith is not muhkam (decisive) and can mean negation of perfection, so it is interpreted accordingly.
Hanafi usul: A khabar wahid cannot override a general Quranic command (amm) to add a specific obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Shafi'i/Maliki: prayer is invalid without al-Fatihah. Hanafi: prayer is valid but deficient; requires sajdat al-sahw if forgetful, and must be repeated if intentional; otherwise the person is sinful.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is wajib, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قراءة الفاتحة أي كلها واجبة فيسجد بترك آية منها، وتعاد وجوبا في العمد والسهو وإن لم يسجد له ولم يعدها يكون آئماً فاسقاً، وعند مالك والشافعي وعند محمد في رواية: فرض؛ لقوله علي: "لا" صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب"، وقوله: "من صلى صلاة لم يقرأ فيها بأم القرآن فهي خداج"، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ ﴾ (المزمل: ٢٠)، والزيادة عليه بخبر الواحد لا تجوز، لكنه يوجب العمل، وقد قلنا به، ومعنى الحديث الأول : لا صلاة كاملة الثواب بدليل قوله علي للأعرابي: "إذا قمت إلى الصلاة فأسبغ الوضوء، ثم استقبل القبلة فكبر، ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن"، فلو كان فرضاً لعلّمه إياها؛ لجهله بالأحكام وحاجته إليها، ولا دلالة في الحديث الثاني؛ لأن الخداج: النقصان، فلا يدل على عدم الجواز بل على النقص، ونحن نقول به، وأيضا الحديث الأول ليس بمحكم بل محتمل لأن يراد به نفي الجواز ونفي الكمال، فتعين الحمل على نفي الكمال بدليل حديث آخر، فلا تجوز به الزيادة ولو كان مشهوراً؛ لأنه ليس محكم. (فتح)
Recitation of al-Fatiha, i.e., all of it, is wajib. So he prostrates (for forgetfulness) if an ayah is omitted. And it must be repeated necessarily in case of intentional and forgetful omission, and if he does not prostrate for it and does not repeat it, he is sinful and a transgressor. And according to Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Muhammad in one narration: it is fard, due to his statement: 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' and his statement: 'Whoever prays a prayer without reciting Umm al-Qur'an in it, it is deficient.' And we have the saying of Allah: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' (73:20). And increasing upon it (the Qur'anic command) by a khabar wahid is not permissible, but it necessitates action, and we have said it. And the meaning of the first hadith: no prayer complete in reward, as evidenced by his statement to the Bedouin: 'When you stand for prayer, perform wudu properly, then face the qibla, say takbir, then recite what is easy from the Qur'an.' So if it were fard, he would have taught it to him, because of his ignorance of the rulings and his need for it. And there is no indication in the second hadith because khadaj means deficiency, so it does not indicate impermissibility but deficiency, and we also say that. Also, the first hadith is not decisive (muhkam) but is probable, because it could be meant to negate permissibility or to negate perfection. So it is determined to mean negation of perfection by another hadith. Thus, increase by it is not allowed even if it is mashhur, because it is not muhkam. (Fath)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in prayer. The Hanafi school maintains that reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard. The proof is the Qur'anic verse commanding to recite what is easy from the Qur'an. The hadiths used by the opposing schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, and Muhammad in a narration) are interpreted as referring to perfection, not obligation. The hadith of the Bedouin shows that the Prophet taught him to recite what is easy, not specifically al-Fatihah, indicating it is not fard. The first hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha' is ambiguous: it could mean no valid prayer or no perfect prayer. The latter is chosen because of other evidence. Therefore, recitation of al-Fatihah is wajib: if omitted, one performs sajdat al-sahw and repeats the prayer if intentional.

Key Terms
خداج (khadāj): Deficient or lacking completeness.
محكم (muḥkam): A decisive text that is unambiguous and cannot be interpreted otherwise.
واجب (wājib): Obligatory but established by speculative (zanni) evidence; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
فرض (farḍ): Obligatory established by decisive (qati) evidence; omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person intentionally omits reciting al-Fatihah in a fard prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but he is sinful and must repeat it.
C) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
D) He must perform sajdat al-sahw and the prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
Reciting Surah al-Fatihah is wajib in prayer, not fard; omission requires sajdat al-sahw and repetition if intentional, but the prayer remains valid.

Adding a Surah after al-Fatihah: The Second Wajib
Ruling that adding a surah after al-Fatihah is the second wajib of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that adding a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib in the Hanafi school, distinguish between fard and wajib in this context, and apply the consequence of omission.

Core Idea
Adding a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard; its omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the absolute act of recitation in prayer is fard, but the specific requirement to recite al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib. Understanding this difference affects how we handle mistakes in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate what the text says about 'adding a surah' and its legal classification. The text explicitly calls it 'the second wajib'.
The phrase 'وهو الواجب الثاني' indicates it is wajib, not fard.
2
Understand the distinction between fard and wajib
The text explains that 'absolute recitation is fard' while 'the particularity of being al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib'. Grasp that fard is the essential obligation, wajib is a required specification.
In Hanafi usul, fard is proven by qati' evidence, wajib by zanni evidence; the consequence differs: omission of fard invalidates prayer, omission of wajib requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) if forgetful.
3
Apply the condition for this wajib
Note that this ruling applies only in rak'ahs where recitation is required: the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and all rak'ahs of nafl prayers.
In the third and fourth rak'ahs of fard, surah is not added; only al-Fatihah is recited.
4
Recognize the consequence of omission
If a person forgets to add a surah, the prayer is still valid but requires sajdah al-sahw. If omitted intentionally, the prayer must be repeated because a wajib was intentionally left.
This distinction is crucial for practical fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضم سورة [ أي مع الفاتحة أو ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة بقدرها وهو الواجب الثاني. (ع ، ط) واعلم أن ضم السورة وإن لم يكن فرضاً بعد ما قرأ الفاتحة لكنه إذا ضمها الفاتحة مع تقع عن الفرض والحاصل أن مطلق القراءة ،فرض وخصوصية كونها فاتحة وسورة واجبة وفي ضمن أداء الواجبين يؤدى الفرض كذا في بعض الشروح.
And adding a surah [i.e., with al-Fatihah, or three short verses, or one long verse equivalent to it, and it is the second wajib. (al-'Inaya, al-Takmilah) And know that adding a surah, even if it is not fard after reciting al-Fatihah, but when he adds it with al-Fatihah, it satisfies the fard. And the summary: that absolute recitation is fard, and the particularity of being al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib. And by performing the two wajibs, the fard is fulfilled. Such is stated in some commentaries.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage states that adding a surah (or equivalent three short verses or one long verse) after al-Fatihah is the second wajib of prayer. The overall obligation (fard) is simply to recite Quran; the specifics of what to recite (al-Fatihah and a surah) are wajib. So by observing these two wajib acts, the underlying fard is fulfilled. The source uses clarifying glosses from al-'Inaya and al-Takmilah.

Key Terms
ضم سورة (ḍamm sūrah): Reciting a surah or equivalent after al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs of fard and in all rak'ahs of nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is mustahab.

Key Takeaway
Adding a surah after al-Fatihah is a wajib act of prayer; its omission requires sajdah al-sahw if forgetful, and repetition if intentional.

Recitation in First Two Rak'ahs of Fard Prayer
Ruling that recitation is specified to the first two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers, cite the proof from the Companions, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard; the last two are optional.

This passage specifies where recitation is required in fard prayers. It clarifies that in three- and four-rak'ah prayers, the obligation of recitation is limited to the first two rak'ahs, with evidence from the practice of the Companions. Understanding this ruling ensures correct observance of salah and prevents unnecessary difficulty in the later rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (recitation in fard prayer) and the specific hukm level (wajib in the first two rak'ahs of three/four-rak'ah prayers; for two-rak'ah Fajr, recitation is fard in both).
The ruling applies to the act of qira'ah within the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib, 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two,' and reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Aisha about choice in the last two.
These are qawl sahabi (statements of Companions).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling: Ali's statement indicates that reciting in the first two fulfills the requirement for the last two, implying no separate obligation for the last two. The reports of choice show that recitation is not mandatory there.
The evidence is zanni (probable) in both transmission and meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i requires recitation in every rak'ah of fard prayers. The passage notes this difference.
The Shafi'i argument is based on general commands to recite.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the specific statements of the Companions, which the school considers stronger evidence in this context. This is the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned; the position is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعيين القراءة: أي في الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي، فقيد 'الأوليين' للاحتراز عن الثنائي، فإنها مطلقا فرض فيهما، والدليل عليها قول علي بن أبي طالب الله : 'القراءة في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين'، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة هما: التخيير في الأخريين إن شاء قرأ وإن شاء سبح. (فتح) الأوليين: أي الركعتين من الفرض، وعند الشافعي: في كل الركعات (ع)
And specification of recitation: i.e., in the four-rak'ah and three-rak'ah fard. So the restriction 'the first two' is to exclude the two-rak'ah (prayer), for in it recitation is fard in both rak'ahs absolutely. The evidence for this is the saying of Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'Recitation in the first two (rak'ahs) is recitation in the last two (rak'ahs).' And from Ibn Mas'ud and Aisha: there is choice in the last two rak'ahs – if he wishes he recites and if he wishes he glorifies (Allah). (Fath) 'The first two' means the two rak'ahs of the fard. And according to al-Shafi'i: in all rak'ahs. (al-'Inaya)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage explains that in fard prayers with three or four rak'ahs (Maghrib, Zuhr, Asr, Isha), recitation of Quran is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs only. The two-rak'ah Fajr prayer is an exception: recitation is fard in both. The proof is a statement of Ali that recitation in the first two is considered recitation for the last two, meaning it suffices. Additionally, Ibn Mas'ud and Aisha reported that one may choose to recite or glorify Allah in the last two rak'ahs. The Shafi'i school differs, requiring recitation in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
تعيين القراءة (ta'yīn al-qirā'ah): The obligation to perform recitation specifically in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) In all four rak'ahs.
B) In the first two rak'ahs only.
C) In the last two rak'ahs only.
D) Only in the first rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers of three or four rak'ahs, not in the last two.

Tranquility in Prayer: Wajib or Fard?
Ruling that tranquility (ta'dil al-arkan) is wajib, with dispute on fardiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies tranquility (tuma'ninah) as wajib rather than fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Tranquility in prayer is wajib, not fard — the Qur'anic command only requires the minimum of the act.

Tranquility in the pillars of prayer — bowing, prostration, standing, and sitting — is a key requirement for proper prayer. But is it a fard, the omission of which invalidates the prayer, or a wajib, which requires compensation? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the two, while Imam al-Shafi'i and even Abu Yusuf from within the Hanafi school consider it fard. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the act in question? It is tranquility (tuma'ninah/ta'dil al-arkan) in each pillar. Who disagrees? Imam al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf say it is fard; the majority Hanafis say it is wajib.
Note that Abu Yusuf's statement is interpreted as 'practical fard' i.e. wajib.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the Qur'anic command 'Bow and prostrate' (22:77). The imperative is fulfilled by the minimal act; additional conditions require a stronger proof. Since no such strong proof exists, tranquility cannot be fard.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf rely on the hadith of the one who prayed poorly, where the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded him to repeat the prayer until he performed it with tranquility. They argue this shows fardiyyah.
The Hanafi response: the hadith indicates necessity (wujub) but not fardiyyah, as it can be interpreted as an obligation short of fard.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf's statement is problematic because he usually does not allow increasing an obligation based on khabar wahid. The text suggests his 'fard' means 'practical fard' i.e. wajib, resolving the conflict.
This shows how Hanafi usul harmonizes apparent contradictions.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If tranquility is fard, omitting it nullifies the prayer (batil). If wajib, the prayer is valid but requires sajdat al-sahw if omitted intentionally. This is the key practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعديل الأركان [ أي تسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود وغيرهما بقدر تسبيحة، وقال الشافعي وأبو يوسف: إنه فرض. (ع)] ووجوب الطمأنينة في الركوع والسجود والقومة والجلسة؛ لمواظبته عليه على ذلك كله، وللأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته حيث قال: ارجع فصل فإنك لم تصل ثلاث مرات ومن هذا قال أبو يوسف والشافعي: إنه فرض، ولنا قوله تعالى: ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا (الحج: ۷۷) أمرنا بالركوع والسجود، فتعلقت الفرضية بالأدنى منهما، وقول أبي يوسف بالفرضية مشكل؛ لأنه جوز ههنا الزيادة بخبر الواحد مع أنها لا تجوز عنده، ولعل قوله محمول على الفرض العملي وهو الواجب فيرتفع الخلاف. (فتح)
And tranquility in the pillars [i.e., calming the limbs in bowing, prostration, and others to the extent of one tasbih. Al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf said: it is fard. (al-'Inaya)] And the obligation of serenity (tuma'ninah) in bowing, prostration, standing after bowing, and sitting; due to his continuous practice of all that, and due to the command in the hadith of the one who prayed poorly where he said: 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed' three times. From this, Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said it is fard. We have His saying: 'Bow and prostrate' (22:77) which commands bowing and prostrating, and the fardiyyah is attached to the minimum of them. And the statement of Abu Yusuf regarding fardiyyah is problematic because he permits here an increase (in obligation) by a khabar wahid while it is not permissible according to him. Perhaps his statement is interpreted as practical fard, i.e., wajib, so the dispute resolves. (Fath)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of tranquility (tuma'ninah) in the pillars of prayer: bowing, prostration, standing after bowing, and sitting. The Hanafi school holds that tranquility is wajib (obligatory but not fard). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i consider it fard. The proof for the Hanafi position is that the Qur'an commands bowing and prostrating, which implies their minimum existence, not necessarily stillness. The hadith of the one who prayed poorly is interpreted as indicating the necessity but not the level of fard. The text suggests that Abu Yusuf might have meant 'practical fard' which is actually wajib, thus resolving the difference.

Key Terms
تعديل الأركان (ta'dīl al-arkān): Performing the pillars of prayer with calmness and stillness, such that the joints settle.
طمأنينة (tuma'nīnah): Serenity, stillness; in prayer, the state of being calm and settled in each posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on tranquility (tuma'ninah) in bowing and prostration?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is mustahab.

Key Takeaway
Tranquility in the pillars of prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, not fard; its intentional omission requires sajdat al-sahw.

Recitation Obligation in First Two Rak'ahs
Ruling on recitation obligation in first two rak'ahs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on recitation in the first two rak'ahs, explain the companion proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the last two suffice with the first two's recitation.

When you stand for a four-rak'ah fard prayer, do you recite Surah al-Fatihah and a surah in every rak'ah? The Hanafi school says no: recitation is required only in the first two. This lesson examines the proof from the Companions and the dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that recitation (qira'ah) is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of four- and three-rak'ah obligatory prayers. Note that in two-rak'ah prayers it is absolutely required in both.
The restriction to 'first two' excludes two-rak'ah prayers.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that recitation is fard (obligatory) in every rak'ah of every prayer.
This is a fundamental difference in the definition of obligation (fard vs. wajib).
3
Understand the Hanafi proof: companion reports
Analyze the proof from 'Ali (ra): 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two' and the reports from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'ishah (ra) allowing choice between recitation and glorification in the last two rak'ahs.
These are qawl sahabi (companion sayings), which are zanni al-thubut and indicate wujub not fard.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i rely on general commands to recite (e.g., 'Read what is easy of the Qur'an') and prophetic practice. The Hanafi response is that the companion reports specify and restrict these general commands to the first two rak'ahs.
The Hanafi use takhsis (specification) of the general command.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In the Hanafi school, omitting recitation in the last two rak'ahs does not invalidate the prayer nor require sajda al-sahw. For Shafi'is, omitting recitation in any rak'ah invalidates the prayer or requires compensation.
The practical consequence is significant for daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعيين القراءة: أي في الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي، فقيد "الأوليين" للاحتراز عن الثنائي، فإنها مطلقا فرض فيهما، والدليل عليها قول علي بن أبي طالب الله : "القراءة في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين"، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة هما: التخيير في الأخريين إن شاء قرأ وإن شاء سبح. (فتح) الأوليين: أي الركعتين من الفرض، وعند الشافعي: في كل الركعات (ع)
And specification of recitation: meaning in the four-rak'ah and three-rak'ah obligatory prayers, the restriction to the first two is to exclude the two-rak'ah prayer, for in it recitation is absolutely obligatory in both. The proof for that is the saying of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him: "Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two." And from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with them: there is choice in the last two; if he wishes he may recite and if he wishes he may glorify. (Fath) 'The first two' meaning the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer, and according to al-Shafi'i: in all the rak'ahs ('Ayni).
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Fath al-Qadir commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It states that in the four- and three-rak'ah obligatory prayers, recitation (of Surah al-Fatihah and a surah) is obligatory only in the first two rak'ahs. The proof is the statement of 'Ali (ra) that recitation in the first two suffices for the last two, and reports from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'ishah (ra) that one may choose to recite or glorify in the last two. Al-Shafi'i holds that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah. The Hanafi position relies on the companion reports showing that the last two rak'ahs do not require recitation. This is a mufta bihi ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الأوليين (al-awwalayn): The first two rak'ahs of a prayer with more than two rak'ahs.
الثنائي (al-thunā'ī): A two-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Fajr).
قراءة (qirā'a): Recitation of Qur'an in prayer, specifically al-Fatihah and a surah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, what is the Hanafi ruling on recitation in the last two rak'ahs?
A) Recitation is fard, required without exception.
B) Recitation is wajib, but one can choose to recite or glorify.
C) Recitation is not required at all; one stands silently.
D) Recitation is sunnah, but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers; the last two do not require recitation.

Order in Repeated Actions: Wajib or Fard?
Inter-madhhab dispute on order in repeated prayer actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on order in repeated actions in prayer and distinguish it from order between different pillars, applying the distinction between fard and wajib.

Core Idea
In prayer, order between different pillars is fard, but order within repeated actions (like two prostrations) is only wajib — sajdat al-sahw suffices.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the ruling on maintaining sequence (tartib) in prayer. While all schools agree that order between distinct actions (e.g., standing before bowing) is obligatory to the point that violating it invalidates the act, there is a disagreement regarding order within repeated actions, such as the two prostrations (sajdahs) of a single rak’ah. The Hanafi school holds that this order is wajib (not fard), meaning prayer remains valid but requires sajdat al-sahw. This nuance arises from the specific nature of the action being repeated.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, clearly state what the Hanafi school holds regarding order in a repeated action (like two sajdahs) within one rak'ah. Note the ruling level (wajib).
The passage explicitly contrasts this with order between different pillars, which is fard by consensus.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Zufar (within Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold this order to be fard. Understand their reasoning: they see any violation of order as fatal to validity.
The passage says 'عند زفر والشافعي: الترتيب في فعل مكرر فرض'.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is not a direct scriptural text but an inductive argument: the fact that sajdat al-sahw is required when a rukn is advanced shows that the order is not fard; if it were fard, sajda would not suffice.
The objection in the passage highlights this: if order were fard, advancing a rukn would invalidate, not just require sajda.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The passage presents an objection: the ruling of sajdat al-sahw for advancing a rukn suggests the violated element is wajib, not fard. The Hanafi response clarifies that the sajda is for delaying the rukn from its proper place, not from another rukn.
This is a subtle point: the second sajda is delayed from its place (after the first sajda), but not from after another pillar.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi, if one reverses the two sajdahs, prayer is valid with sajdat al-sahw. In Shafi'i/Zufar's view, prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This difference matters in daily practice, especially for those who follow different schools in their congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورعاية الترتيب: وعند زفر والشافعي: الترتيب في فعل مكرر فرض، أما رعاية الترتيب بين الأفعال المكرّرة في الركعتين وما فوقهما ففرض اتفاقاً كترتيب القيام على الركوع وترتيب الركوع على السجود، أي يتوقف صحة الثاني على وجود الأول حتى لو ركع بعد السجود لم يعتد بالسجود، فعليه إعادة السجود، فإن قيل: الحكم بفرضية الترتيب ينافي قولهم في سجدة السهو من أن تقديم ركن يوجبها؛ لأن هذا شأن الواجب، فالجواب أن السجدة إنما هي لتأخير الركن عن محله لا لتأخيره عن ركن آخر. (فتح) مكرّر: في ركعة واحدة كالسجدة حتى لو نسي سجدة من الأولى قضاها ولو بعد السلام وسجد للسهو. (ع)
And observing order: while with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, order in a repeated action is fard. As for observing order between repeated actions in two rak'ahs and above, it is fard by consensus, like the order of standing before bowing and the order of bowing before prostration. That is, the validity of the second depends on the existence of the first, such that if he bowed after prostration, the prostration is not counted, and he must repeat the prostration. If it is said: the ruling of the fardiyyah of order contradicts their statement concerning sajdat al-sahw that advancing an integral necessitates it, because that is the characteristic of an obligatory act, the answer is that the sajda is only for delaying the integral from its place, not for delaying it from another integral. (Fath) 'Repeated' refers to what is in one rak'ah like the prostration, so that if he forgets a prostration from the first [rak'ah] he makes it up even after the salutation and prostrates for forgetfulness. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage from Fath al-Qadir explains the Hanafi ruling on order (tartib) in prayer. It distinguishes two types: (1) order between different pillars within the same rak'ah (e.g., standing before bowing, bowing before prostration) – this is fard by consensus. (2) order between repeated actions, such as two prostrations within one rak'ah – here, Hanafis hold it is wajib (not fard), while Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold it is fard. The commentary argues that if order were fard in a repeated action, then advancing a prostration would invalidate the rak'ah, but the Hanafi ruling that sajdat al-sahw suffices shows it is only wajib. The sajda compensates for delaying the second prostration from its proper place, not from another pillar. The term 'repeated' here refers to actions within one rak'ah, such as the two sajdas. If one forgets a sajda, they perform it after the salam and do sajdat al-sahw.

Key Terms
الترتيب في فعل مكرر (al-tartib fi fi'l mukrar): Order between two occurrences of the same type of action within a rak'ah, e.g., the two prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone prostrates twice but then realizes they did the first prostration after the second (i.e., reversed the two sajdas), what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but sajdat al-sahw is required.
C) The prayer is valid without any compensation.
D) The rak'ah must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi, order between repeated actions like two prostrations is wajib, not fard, because sajdat al-sahw compensates for the delay.

The First Sitting and Tashahhud: Wajib, Not Fard
Rulings on the first sitting and tashahhud with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi evidence for the wujub of the first sitting and tashahhud, and evaluate the Shafi'i position that they are fard.

Core Idea
The first sitting and tashahhud are wajib; the Prophet's forgetting without returning proves non-fardiyyah.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the rulings of the first sitting and tashahhud in salah. While many assume these are merely sunnah, the Hanafi school holds them as wajib. Understanding the evidence—the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) and his forgetting incident—reveals the precision of Hanafi usul in distinguishing between fard and wajib. This lesson dissects the proof and the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling for the first sitting and tashahhud in the Hanafi school?
It is wajib in all prayers of three or more rak'ahs.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which scholars consider it fard?
Muhammad, Zufar (intra-Hanafi) and al-Shafi'i (inter-madhhab) consider it fard in specific contexts.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What evidence do the opponents cite?
The general command to sit and recite tashahhud, indicating fardiyyah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this?
The command indicates wujub, not fard; the Prophet's forgetting and not returning to the sitting proves it is not fard.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings?
Hanafi: omission requires sajdat al-sahw; Shafi'i: omission may invalidate the prayer (if fard omitted).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقعود الأول: [ولو في نفل على الأصح، وأراد بالأول غير الأخير. (ط)] للمواظبة، ولأنه عليها سها عنه فلم يعد إليه، فبالمواظبة استفيد الوجوب، وبعدم عوده إليه استفيد عدمُ الفرضية، وأكثر مشايخنا يطلقون عليه اسم السنة إما لأن وجوبه ثبت بالسنة أو لأن المؤكدة في معنى الواجب، وهذا يقتضي رفع الخلاف، والمراد بالأول مطلقاً سواء كان في الرباعية أو الثلاثية أو الفرض أو النفل، وعند محمد وزفر والشافعي: القعدة الأولى في الرباعي من النفل فرض. (مسكين، فتح والتشهد [ أي والسابع قراءة التشهد مطلقاً سواء كان في الأولى أو في الثانية، وقال الشافعي: في الثانية فرض (مسكين)] وفي "المحيط": التشهد في القعدتين واجب؛ لأنه عليه قرأه فيهما، وأمرهم به، دل ذلك على الوجوب دون الفرضية، وفي اقتصاره على التشهد إيماء إلى عدم وجوب الصلاة عليه في القعود الأخير، بل هي سنة فقط على ما سيأتي في المتن، ووجوب قراءته هو ظاهر الرواية فلذلك أطلق والقياس أن يكون سنة في الأولى، وهو اختيار البعض. (عيني، فتح)
And the first sitting: [even in a supererogatory prayer according to the most correct view, and by 'first' he means other than the last. (Tabyin)] Due to continuous practice, and because he (peace be upon him) forgot it and did not return to it; by continuous practice obligation is derived, and by not returning to it the non-obligatoriness (as fard) is derived. Most of our scholars call it sunnah, either because its obligation is established by the sunnah or because the emphatically recommended is in the meaning of wajib. This entails the removal of disagreement. And by 'first' is meant generally, whether in a four-rak'ah, three-rak'ah, obligatory or supererogatory prayer. According to Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i: the first sitting in four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer is fard. (Miskin, Fath) And the tashahhud: [meaning the seventh [part] is the recitation of the tashahhud absolutely, whether in the first or the second. Al-Shafi'i said: in the second it is fard. (Miskin)] And in al-Muhit: the tashahhud in both sittings is wajib; because he (peace be upon him) recited it in both and commanded them to do so; that indicates wujub, not fardiyyah. And his restricting himself to tashahhud hints at the non-obligation of sending blessings upon him in the last sitting; rather it is only sunnah, as will come in the text. And the obligation of reciting it is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) therefore he [the author] made it absolute, but by analogy it would be sunnah in the first, and that is the choice of some. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: the first sitting (al-qu'ud al-awwal) and the recitation of tashahhud. For the first sitting, the Hanafi position is that it is wajib in all prayers (obligatory and supererogatory) that have more than two rak'ahs. Evidence: the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates wujub, and the fact that he forgot it once and did not return to it shows it is not fard. Most Hanafi scholars call it sunnah, meaning mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah), which in effect is wajib. Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i consider it fard in the four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer. For tashahhud, it is wajib in both the first and second sittings according to zahir al-riwayah. The Prophet recited it and commanded it, indicating wujub. Some scholars, by analogy, say it is sunnah in the first sitting. Al-Shafi'i holds it is fard in the last sitting. The passage also notes that sending blessings on the Prophet (salat 'ala al-nabi) in the last sitting is only sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The sitting after the second rak'ah in prayers with more than two rak'ahs.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, etc.) during the sitting in salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard; omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib; omitting it requires sajdat al-sahw.
C) It is sunnah; no compensation needed.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
The first sitting and tashahhud are wajib in Hanafi fiqh; omitting them requires sajdat al-sahw, not repetition of the prayer.
