Salat upon the Prophet in Tashahhud: Sunnah or Fard?
Dispute on obligation of salat in tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat in the last tashahhud, explain the opposing Shafi'i view, and evaluate the proofs from both sides.

Core Idea
Sending blessings upon the Prophet in the last tashahhud is sunnah in the Hanafi school, not fard, despite the Quranic command.

A key inter-madhhab dispute arises over whether sending blessings (salat) upon the Prophet in the final sitting of prayer is obligatory or recommended. The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools consider it fard. This lesson examines the primary proofs and the Hanafi response, clarifying the practical consequence for a Hanafi worshipper.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling (sunnah) and the context (last tashahhud). Note that the Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The Shafi'i school argues that the Quranic command 'Sallu 'alayhi' (al-Ahzab:56) and the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not send blessings' make it fard. Highlight these proofs.
Other schools (Maliki, Hanbali) follow similar reasoning.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Quran
The Hanafi response: the command is fulfilled once in a lifetime by saying 'al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabi' in tashahhud. The command does not necessitate repetition.
The principle: al-amr la yaqtadi al-takrar.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Bedouin hadith
When the Prophet taught a Bedouin the obligations of prayer, he did not mention salat, indicating it is not an obligation.
This is a key dalil: the Prophet's action (tark) shows non-obligation.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If omitted, the Hanafi prayer is valid but incomplete; in the Shafi'i school, it becomes invalid if intentionally omitted.
This difference affects fatwa and practice for followers of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلاة على النبي والدعاء. والصلاة إلخ: أي في القعدة الأخيرة سنة عندنا، وعند الشافعي فرض؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ﴾ (الأحزاب: ٥٦)، والأمر للوجوب، ولا تجب خارج الصلاة فتعينت في الصلاة، ولنا أنه عليه السلام علم أعرابياً فرائض الصلاة، ولم يعلمه الصلاة عليه, فلو كانت فرضاً لعلّمه إياها، وليس في الآية دلالة على ما قال؛ لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار بل تجب في العمر مرة، وقد وفينا بموجب الأمر بقولنا: السلام عليك أيها النبي، فلا تجب ثانياً في ذلك المجلس؛ إذ لو وجب لما فرغ لعبادة أخرى؛ لأن الصلاة عليه لا تخلو عن ذكره عليه السلام فيكتفي بمرة في مجلس. تبيين الحقائق: ٢٨١/١، ٢٨٢] وقوله عليه السلام: "لا صلاة لمن لم يصل علي في صلاته" محمول على نفي الكمال، وقال أبو حنيفة: لا يصلّي على غير الأنبياء إلا على آله عليه السلام أثر ذلك؛ لأن فيه تعظيماً له، ومن سنن رفع سبابة اليمنى في التشهد عند "أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله" وهو المفتى به. (فتح، مسكين) على النبي : أي بعد التشهد الأخير، وقال الشافعي: هي فرض وبه قال مالك وأحمد. (ع)
And sending blessings upon the Prophet and supplication. And 'sending blessings' etc.: i.e., in the last sitting it is sunnah with us, while with al-Shafi'i it is fard, due to His statement, the Exalted: {Send blessings upon him} (al-Ahzab: 56), and a command indicates obligation, and it is not obligatory outside the prayer, so it is determined in the prayer. And our proof is that he (peace be upon him) taught a Bedouin the obligations of prayer, and did not teach him sending blessings upon him. If it were obligatory, he would have taught it to him. And there is no indication in the verse for what he said, because the command does not necessitate repetition; rather it is obligatory once in a lifetime, and we have fulfilled the requirement of the command by our saying: 'Peace be upon you, O Prophet.' So it is not obligatory a second time in that sitting; for if it were obligatory, he would not have turned to another act of worship, because sending blessings upon him does not cease to include mentioning him (peace be upon him) and once suffices in a session. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 281/1, 282. And his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no prayer for one who does not send blessings upon me in his prayer' is interpreted as negation of perfection. And Abu Hanifa said: One does not send blessings upon other than the prophets except upon the family of the Prophet (peace be upon him) following that, because it is glorification of him. And from the sunan is raising the right index finger in tashahhud when saying 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah', and that is the mufta bihi. (Fath, Miskin) 'Upon the Prophet': i.e., after the final tashahhud. Al-Shafi'i said it is fard, and Malik and Ahmad also said that. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of sending blessings (salat) upon the Prophet during the last sitting of prayer. The Hanafi school considers it sunnah, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools consider it fard (obligatory). The Hanafi proof is that when the Prophet taught a Bedouin the essentials of prayer, he did not include sending blessings upon himself, indicating it is not obligatory. The Shafi'i proof from the Quranic command (al-Ahzab:56) is countered by the Hanafi argument that the command is for once in a lifetime, and it is fulfilled by the salutation already said in tashahhud (al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabi). The hadith 'No prayer for one who does not send blessings' is interpreted as meaning the prayer is incomplete, not invalid. Additionally, the text notes that according to Abu Hanifa, sending blessings is only for prophets and their families, not other individuals, because it implies glorification. The sunnah of raising the index finger in tashahhud is also mentioned.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-ṣalāh 'alā al-nabī): Sending blessings and peace upon the Prophet Muhammad, usually saying 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer, after the last sujud, before the closing salutation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sending blessings upon the Prophet in the last tashahhud is an emphasized sunnah, not an obligation — omission does not invalidate the prayer.

Du'a After Tashahhud: Content and Conditions
Ruling on du'a after tashahhud with content conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on du'a after tashahhud and identify which types of supplications are permitted or prohibited.

Core Idea
Du'a in prayer must resemble Quranic speech; worldly requests invalidate it.

After completing the tashahhud, it is sunnah to make du'a. However, the Hanafi school places a critical condition: the du'a must use phrases that resemble the Quran and transmitted supplications. Requests that could be made of people, such as asking for a spouse, are prohibited and invalidate the prayer. This lesson examines the proof and the disagreement with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is du'a after tashahhud. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory. The sunnah includes specific content: it should be for believers, oneself, and parents, using Quran-like phrases.
Sunnah muakkadah: strongly recommended, omission disliked but not sinful.
2
Locate the condition and its proof
The condition: du'a must not include speech that resembles kalām al-nās (human conversation), defined as requests that could be asked of people. The proof is the hadith: 'Our prayer is not suitable for any of the speech of people.'
Examples of prohibited: 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so' or 'Give me a house.'
3
Understand the madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik permit any permissible du'a, including worldly requests, based on the hadith 'Ask Allah for your needs, even the strap of your sandals.' The Hanafi response interprets this hadith as applying outside prayer.
Thamarah al-khilaf: the same du'a may invalidate prayer in the Hanafi school but not in the Shafi'i or Maliki.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a scenario where someone in prayer says 'O Allah, give me a job,' determine the ruling. According to Hanafi, this is kalām al-nās (can be asked of people) and invalidates the prayer. According to Shafi'i, it is valid.
Always check if the request is something normally asked of humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح)
And supplication: the twenty-third (sunnah): supplication when he finishes the tashahhud for the believing men and believing women, and for himself and his parents, with words resembling the expressions of the Quran and transmitted supplications, because al-Tirmidhi authenticated as marfu': It was said: O Messenger of Allah, which supplication is most heard? He said: 'The last part of the night and after the obligatory prayer,' i.e., before finishing it. And he should not supplicate with words that resemble the speech of people. And it is interpreted as that which is impossible to ask from people, such as: 'O Allah, give me such-and-such' and 'Marry me to a woman.' According to al-Shafi'i and Malik, everything that is permissible to supplicate with outside prayer does not invalidate the prayer, such as saying: 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so,' due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Ask Allah for your needs, even the strap of your sandals and the salt for your pots.' Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of making du'a after the final tashahhud. The Hanafi school holds that du'a is sunnah and should use phrases resembling Quranic supplications and transmitted prayers. It is recommended to supplicate for believers, oneself, and parents. The du'a should not include requests that are plausible in human speech (like 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so'), because prayer is not for worldly speech that could be asked of people. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools allow any permissible du'a, including asking for marriage, based on the hadith 'Ask Allah for your needs.' The Hanafi response uses the hadith 'Our prayer is not suitable for any of the speech of people,' and interprets the other hadith as applying outside prayer. Additionally, the text mentions the sunnah of raising hands in du'a (palms facing the face) and wiping the face at the end.

Key Terms
دبر المكتوبة (dubur al-maktūbah): After the obligatory prayer, specifically before the closing salutation according to some interpretations.
كلام الناس (kalām al-nās): Speech that is characteristic of human conversation, including asking for things normally asked of people.
الدعاء المأثور (al-du'ā' al-ma'thūr): Supplications transmitted from the Prophet or the Quran.

Sunnahs of Sitting and the Ruling on Qawmah/Jalsah
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on sitting and standing postures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnahs of sitting in prayer (iftirash) and explain the legal dispute on qawmah and jalsah, distinguishing between fard and wajib and their practical consequences.

Core Idea
Iftirash is sunnah in all sittings; qawmah and jalsah are wajib, not fard — omission requires sujud al-sahw, not invalidation.

The Prophet's prayer included specific sitting postures and brief standings. The Hanafi school prescribes iftirash in all sittings and considers the standing after ruku' (qawmah) and sitting between prostrations (jalsah) as wajib — obligatory but not at the level of fard. This lesson examines the evidence and the inter-madhhab dispute, particularly with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i who consider these elements fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnahs of sitting
State the Hanafi ruling: the worshipper should sit on his left foot with the right foot erect (iftirash) in all sittings, including between prostrations and during tashahhud.
This is based on hadith from Aisha and Anas.
2
Understand the prohibition of tawarruk
Note that tawarruk (sitting on buttocks with legs to the side) is prohibited in Hanafi view, except for excuse. The Prophet's tawarruk in old age is interpreted as due to weakness.
Shafi'i and Maliki schools prescribe tawarruk in the final sitting.
3
Recognize the ikhtilaf on qawmah and jalsah
According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, qawmah and jalsah are fard (omission invalidates prayer). In the narration of al-Karkhi, they are wajib (omission requires sujud al-sahw).
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that they are wajib.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if omitted intentionally, Hanafi prayer is still valid (with sin and sujud al-sahw), while Shafi'i prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This shows the importance of the fard/wajib distinction in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position: qawmah and jalsah are wajib. If omitted forgetfully, sujud al-sahw is required; if omitted intentionally, the prayer is makruh tahrimi but still valid, and sujud al-sahw is still needed.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الصلاة: وافتراش رجله اليسرى ونصب اليمنى، والقومة والجلسة. شرح: وافتراش رجله إلخ: أي مطلقا؛ لأنه لو فعل كذلك كما روي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا قعد فرش رجله اليسرى وقعد عليها ونصب رجله اليمنى، وعن أنس رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن التورك، وهو أن يضع إليتيه على الأرض، ويخرج رجليه إلى الجانب الأيمن، وما احتج به الشافعي ومالك في توركه عليه فمحمول على ضعفه وكبر سنه، وكذا يفترش بين السجدتين. (فتح، مستخلص) نصب اليمنى في حالة القعود للتشهد في القعدتين، وعند الشافعي وأحمد: يتورك في الآخرة، وعند مالك: يتورك فيهما. (ع) والقومة: القومة بين الركوع والسجود، وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي: القومة والجلسة فرضان حتى لو ترك القومة أو الجلسة فسدت صلاته، وفي رواية الكرخي: هما واجبان، وكذلك رفع الرأس من الركوع والانتصاب والطمأنينة، ولو ترك شيئا من ذلك ساهياً يلزمه سجود السهو. (فتح) والجلسة: الجلسة بين السجدتين، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: هما فرض. (ع)
The sunnahs of prayer: spreading his left foot and erecting the right, and the standing and sitting. Explanation: 'spreading his foot etc.' means absolutely; because he did that as narrated from Aisha that the Prophet, when he sat, spread his left foot and sat on it and erected his right foot, and from Anas that the Prophet forbade tawarruk, which is to place his buttocks on the ground and extend his legs to the right side. What al-Shafi'i and Malik argued regarding his tawarruk is interpreted as due to his weakness and old age. Likewise, he spreads between the two prostrations. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Erecting the right foot while sitting for tashahhud in both sittings; according to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad: he does tawarruk in the last sitting; and according to Malik: he does tawarruk in both. (Ayni) And the standing: the standing between bowing and prostration. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: the standing and sitting are obligatory such that if one omits the standing or sitting, his prayer is invalidated. In the narration of al-Karkhi: both are wajib. Likewise, raising the head from bowing, standing upright, and tranquility. If one omits any of that forgetfully, he is required to perform the prostration of forgetfulness. (Fath) And the sitting: the sitting between the two prostrations; Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: both are fard. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi sunnahs of sitting in prayer and the disputed rulings on qawmah (standing after ruku') and jalsah (sitting between prostrations). The author first states the ruling: the worshipper should spread his left foot and sit on it, and erect the right foot (iftirash). This applies in all sittings, including between prostrations and in tashahhud. The evidence is from hadith of Aisha and Anas. The hadith of Anas prohibits tawarruk (sitting on the buttocks with legs to one side), which is used by Shafi'i and Malik, but the Hanafi position interprets that as due to the Prophet's old age and weakness. Then the passage discusses qawmah and jalsah: according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, these are fard (obligatory), while in the narration of al-Karkhi they are wajib, which is the Hanafi relied-upon position. The difference between fard and wajib in Hanafi school is that fard is proven by definitive evidence, while wajib is proven by probable evidence; omission of wajib requires sujud al-sahw, not repetition of prayer. The passage notes that even according to Abu Yusuf, the prayer is invalidated if qawmah or jalsah is omitted intentionally, but forgetfully only sujud al-sahw is needed.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirāsh): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect; the recommended sitting posture in prayer.
تورك (tawarruk): Sitting on the buttocks with legs extended to the right side; this is prohibited in Hanafi view except for excuse.
القومة (al-qawmah): Standing upright after rising from ruku', before going into sujud.
الجلسة (al-jalsah): Sitting between the two prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib, and forgetting it requires sujud al-sahw.
C) It is sunnah, and omitting it is permissible without any action.
D) It is makruh, and omitting it is recommended.

Key Takeaway
Qawmah and jalsah are wajib in Hanafi prayer; intentional or forgetful omission requires sujud al-sahw, but the prayer is not invalidated.

Du'a After Tashahhud: Hanafi Restrictions vs. Shafi'i/Maliki Permissiveness
Ruling on du'a content after tashahhud and madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on du'a after tashahhud and explain the disagreement with the Shafi'i/Maliki schools regarding permissible content, citing the key evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Worldly requests in prayer invalidate it (Hanafi); Shafi'is permit them.

This lesson examines a classic dispute about what kinds of supplications are permitted during the prayer after tashahhud. The Hanafi school maintains a strict boundary, while other schools allow more freedom. Understanding this disagreement requires careful analysis of two competing hadiths.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (du'a after tashahhud) and the Hanafi ruling: only Quranic and transmitted supplications are allowed; worldly requests invalidate the prayer.
2
Identify the opposing view
Shafi'i and Malik hold that any permissible du'a (including worldly requests) does not invalidate the prayer.
Based on the general hadith encouraging asking for needs.
3
Analyze each proof
Hanafi proof: hadith 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people.' Shafi'i/Maliki proof: hadith 'Ask Allah for your needs even for the thong of your sandals.' Determine how each school interprets these texts.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the 'Ask Allah' hadith applies to du'a outside prayer, not within. The 'speech of people' hadith is decisive for prayer context.
This is an example of takhsis (specification) of a general command by a more specific ruling.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi school, saying 'O Allah marry me to so-and-so' invalidates the prayer; in Shafi'i/Maliki, it does not.
This highlights how usul differences lead to different fiqh outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدعاء: الدعاء إذا فرغ من التشهد للمؤمنين والمؤمنات ولنفسه ولوالديه بما يشبه ألفاظ القرآن والأدعية المأثورة لما حسنه الترمذي مرفوعاً: قيل : يا رسول الله أيّ الدعاء أسمع؟ قال: "جوف الليل الأخير و دبر المكتوبة" أي قبل الفراغ منه، ولا يدعو بما يشبه كلام الناس، وفسر بما لا يستحيل سؤاله من الناس نحو: اللهم أعطني كذا وزوجني امرأة وعند الشافعي ومالك كل ما ساغ الدعاء به خارج الصلاة لا يفسد الصلاة نحو أن يقول: اللهم زوجني فلانة؛ لقوله عليه: "سلوا الله حوائجكم حتى الشسع لنعالكم والملح لقدوركم"، ولنا قوله عليه: "إن صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس"، ولا دلالة فيما رواه أنه في الصلاة، فيحمل على الدعاء خارجاً، السنة: رفع الأيدي في الدعاء حذاء الصدر، وبطونها مما يلي الوجه، منها: ومن بقوله: "سبحان ربك" إلى رب العالمين، ومنها: أن يمسح بيديه وجهه في آخره أي عند الفراغ عنه. (فتح)
And supplication: The supplication when he finishes from the tashahhud for the believing men and women, for himself and his parents, with words resembling the Qur'an and transmitted supplications, because al-Tirmidhi has classified it as hasan from the Prophet: It was said, 'O Messenger of Allah, which supplication is most likely to be heard?' He said: 'The last part of the night and after the prescribed prayer' meaning before its completion. And he should not supplicate with words resembling the speech of people, and it is interpreted as what it is not impossible to ask from people, such as 'O Allah, give me such and such and marry me such woman.' According to al-Shafi'i and Malik, any supplication that is permissible outside prayer does not invalidate the prayer, such as saying 'O Allah, marry me so-and-so', due to his saying: 'Ask Allah for your needs, even for the thong of your sandals and salt for your pots.' Our proof is his saying: 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people,' and there is no indication in the hadith that it is in the prayer, so it is interpreted as supplication outside. The sunnah: raising hands in supplication at chest level with palms facing the face, including from his saying 'Subhana rabbika' to 'al-'alamin', and including wiping his hands over his face at the end, meaning when finishing it. (Fath)
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the du'a after tashahhud. The recommended du'a is for believers, oneself, and parents, using phrases similar to the Qur'an and transmitted du'as. The evidence is the hadith that the best du'a is 'the last part of the night and after the prescribed prayer', meaning before ending the prayer. However, the Hanafi school prohibits making du'a with words that resemble ordinary human speech, such as asking for specific worldly items like marriage to a named person. Imam al-Shafi'i and Malik argue that any du'a permissible outside prayer is also permissible inside, based on the hadith 'Ask Allah for your needs even for the thong of your sandals.' The Hanafi response distinguishes by citing the hadith 'This prayer of ours is not suitable for any of the speech of people.' They argue that the hadith about asking for sandals is referring to du'a outside prayer. Therefore, within prayer, only Quranic and transmitted du'as are allowed. The passage also mentions the sunnah of raising hands in du'a at chest level, palms facing the face, and wiping the face at the end. These are recommended practices.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-duʿāʾ): Supplication after tashahhud, preferably in Quranic and transmitted phrases.
كلام الناس (kalām al-nās): Human speech; ordinary conversation not fitting for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No effect on prayer.

Key Takeaway
Worldly requests in du'a after tashahhud invalidate the prayer in the Hanafi school, based on the specific prohibition of human speech in prayer.

The Concept of Adab in Prayer
Lists and explains the first three etiquettes of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of adab as sunnah muakkadah and explain the consequence of omitting them.

Core Idea
Adab are recommended etiquettes; omitting them loses reward but does not invalidate prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, adab are sunnah muakkadah – strongly recommended actions that enhance the prayer. They are not obligatory, so the prayer remains valid even if neglected. This lesson establishes the general ruling and the importance of observing these etiquettes for spiritual benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fiqh category
The term adab indicates these are sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
2
Understand the hukm level
Sunnah muakkadah: omission is makruh tanzih but prayer is valid.
3
Apply to the three etiquettes
All three etiquettes listed (gaze, yawn, hands) fall under this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الصلاة وآدابها: نظره إلى موضع سجوده، وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب، وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير. شرح: آدابها: أي آداب الصلاة ستة على ما ذكره، الأوّل: نظره أي نظر المصلي إلى موضع سجوده قائماً وإلى قدميه راكعاً، وإلى حجره قاعداً، وإلى أرنبة أنفه ساجداً، وإلى منكبه الأيمن والأيسر حالة التسليمتين. (ط) وكظم فمه: أي إمساكه ولو يأخذ شفة بأسنانه خوفاً من ضحك الشيطان منه بفعله؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده بيده ما استطاع، فإن أحدكم إذا تثاءب ضحك منه الشيطان"، وكأنه فيه من التكاسل فيما محله النشاط والخضوع والتثاؤب مهموز كما في المصباح. (فتح) التثاؤب: لأنه من الشيطان وإن تعذر يضع ظهر الكف على الفم. وإخراج كفيه: لأنه أقرب للتواضع، وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة، وأمكن من نشر الأصابع، وهذا في حق الرجال، وأما في حق النساء فجعل يديها في كميها؛ لأنه أسترلها. (فتح) عند التكبير: أي عند التكبير الأول إلا لضرورة كبرد وأما المرأة فتجعل في كميها ما استطاع: يعني مهما أمكن؛ لأنه ليس من أفعال الصلاة، ولو كان بلا عذر فحصلت منه حروف تفسد صلاته. (ع)
And its etiquettes: his gaze at the place of his prostration, and suppressing his mouth at yawning, and taking out his palms from his sleeves at the takbir. Explanation: 'Its etiquettes' i.e. the etiquettes of prayer are six as mentioned. The first: his gaze i.e. the gaze of the worshipper at his prostration spot while standing, to his feet while bowing, to his lap while sitting, to the tip of his nose while prostrating, and to his right and left shoulders during the two salutations. (Tahavi) And suppressing his mouth: i.e. restraining it, even by taking his lip with his teeth, for fear of Satan laughing at him due to his action; because of his saying: 'When one of you yawns, let him suppress it with his hand as much as he can, for indeed when one of you yawns, Satan laughs at him.' And it seems there is laziness in a place that requires activity and humility, and 'tathā'ub' (yawning) is with a hamza as in al-Misbah. (Fath) Yawning: because it is from Satan, and if it is difficult, he places the back of his hand on his mouth. And taking out his palms: because it is closer to humility, further from resembling the tyrants, and more capable of spreading the fingers. This applies to men; as for women, they place their hands inside their sleeves because it is more covering. (Fath) At the takbir: meaning at the first takbir, except for necessity like cold. And a woman places her hands in her sleeves as much as possible: meaning as much as possible, because it is not from the actions of prayer, and if it is done without excuse and letters come out of it, it invalidates his prayer. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage explains the first three etiquettes (adab) of prayer as listed by the author. The first is that the worshipper should look at the place of prostration while standing, at his feet while bowing, at his lap while sitting, at the tip of his nose while prostrating, and at his right and left shoulders during the two salutations. This helps maintain focus and humility. The second etiquette is to suppress a yawn as much as possible, even by biting the lip, because yawning is from Satan and suggests laziness; the hadith indicates Satan laughs at the person who yawns. If one cannot suppress it, one should place the back of the hand over the mouth. The third etiquette is for men to remove their hands from their sleeves when raising the hands for the opening takbir, as this shows humility and avoids resembling arrogant people. It also allows proper spreading of fingers. For women, they keep their hands inside the sleeves for greater modesty, except in cases of necessity like extreme cold. The passage notes that if one without excuse makes sounds (letters) when changing hand positions, it could invalidate the prayer if it produces clear speech.

Key Terms
آداب الصلاة (ādāb al-ṣalāh): Recommended etiquettes of prayer that enhance humility and focus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer being invalid.
B) The prayer being valid but disliked.
C) The prayer being completely fine without any dislike.
D) The prayer needing to be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Adab are sunnah; observing them perfects the prayer but omitting them does not break it.

The Gaze in Prayer
Explains the first adab of gaze in detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended direction of gaze in each posture of prayer according to Hanafi adab.

Core Idea
Gaze at the prostration spot while standing, feet while bowing, lap while sitting, nose tip while prostrating, shoulders during salams.

The first adab is controlling the gaze. The worshipper's eyes should be directed to specific places to maintain concentration and humility. This lesson details where to look in each posture.

Guided Path
1
Recall the five postures
Standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting, and salams.
2
State the gaze for each
Standing: prostration spot; bowing: feet; sitting: lap; prostrating: nose tip; salams: shoulders.
3
Understand the wisdom
Fixed gaze prevents distraction and fosters khushu.

Source Text

آداب الصلاة وآدابها: نظره إلى موضع سجوده، وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب، وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير. شرح: آدابها: أي آداب الصلاة ستة على ما ذكره، الأوّل: نظره أي نظر المصلي إلى موضع سجوده قائماً وإلى قدميه راكعاً، وإلى حجره قاعداً، وإلى أرنبة أنفه ساجداً، وإلى منكبه الأيمن والأيسر حالة التسليمتين. (ط) وكظم فمه: أي إمساكه ولو يأخذ شفة بأسنانه خوفاً من ضحك الشيطان منه بفعله؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده بيده ما استطاع، فإن أحدكم إذا تثاءب ضحك منه الشيطان"، وكأنه فيه من التكاسل فيما محله النشاط والخضوع والتثاؤب مهموز كما في المصباح. (فتح) التثاؤب: لأنه من الشيطان وإن تعذر يضع ظهر الكف على الفم. وإخراج كفيه: لأنه أقرب للتواضع، وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة، وأمكن من نشر الأصابع، وهذا في حق الرجال، وأما في حق النساء فجعل يديها في كميها؛ لأنه أسترلها. (فتح) عند التكبير: أي عند التكبير الأول إلا لضرورة كبرد وأما المرأة فتجعل في كميها ما استطاع: يعني مهما أمكن؛ لأنه ليس من أفعال الصلاة، ولو كان بلا عذر فحصلت منه حروف تفسد صلاته. (ع)
And its etiquettes: his gaze at the place of his prostration, and suppressing his mouth at yawning, and taking out his palms from his sleeves at the takbir. Explanation: 'Its etiquettes' i.e. the etiquettes of prayer are six as mentioned. The first: his gaze i.e. the gaze of the worshipper at his prostration spot while standing, to his feet while bowing, to his lap while sitting, to the tip of his nose while prostrating, and to his right and left shoulders during the two salutations. (Tahavi) And suppressing his mouth: i.e. restraining it, even by taking his lip with his teeth, for fear of Satan laughing at him due to his action; because of his saying: 'When one of you yawns, let him suppress it with his hand as much as he can, for indeed when one of you yawns, Satan laughs at him.' And it seems there is laziness in a place that requires activity and humility, and 'tathā'ub' (yawning) is with a hamza as in al-Misbah. (Fath) Yawning: because it is from Satan, and if it is difficult, he places the back of his hand on his mouth. And taking out his palms: because it is closer to humility, further from resembling the tyrants, and more capable of spreading the fingers. This applies to men; as for women, they place their hands inside their sleeves because it is more covering. (Fath) At the takbir: meaning at the first takbir, except for necessity like cold. And a woman places her hands in her sleeves as much as possible: meaning as much as possible, because it is not from the actions of prayer, and if it is done without excuse and letters come out of it, it invalidates his prayer. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage explains the first three etiquettes (adab) of prayer as listed by the author. The first is that the worshipper should look at the place of prostration while standing, at his feet while bowing, at his lap while sitting, at the tip of his nose while prostrating, and at his right and left shoulders during the two salutations. This helps maintain focus and humility. The second etiquette is to suppress a yawn as much as possible, even by biting the lip, because yawning is from Satan and suggests laziness; the hadith indicates Satan laughs at the person who yawns. If one cannot suppress it, one should place the back of the hand over the mouth. The third etiquette is for men to remove their hands from their sleeves when raising the hands for the opening takbir, as this shows humility and avoids resembling arrogant people. It also allows proper spreading of fingers. For women, they keep their hands inside the sleeves for greater modesty, except in cases of necessity like extreme cold. The passage notes that if one without excuse makes sounds (letters) when changing hand positions, it could invalidate the prayer if it produces clear speech.

Key Terms
النظر (al-nazar): The gaze; direction of the eyes during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The place of prostration.
B) The tip of his nose.
C) His hands.
D) His feet.

Key Takeaway
Gaze placement is a sunnah that aids khushu in each posture.

Suppressing Yawns in Prayer
Explains the second adab of yawning with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi adab for yawning in prayer and the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Suppress a yawn by biting your lip or placing the back of your hand on your mouth; yawning is from Shaytan.

Yawning is a natural response but in prayer it is disliked because it indicates laziness. The Prophet ﷺ instructed us to suppress it. This lesson covers the method and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Recognize that yawning is from Shaytan
The hadith states that Shaytan laughs at the person who yawns.
2
Know the recommended response
Suppress by biting lip or with hand; if difficult, use back of hand.
3
Apply during prayer
This adab is particularly important in prayer to maintain focus and humility.

Removing Hands from Sleeves at Takbir
Explains the third adab of removing hands with gender distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rule for men vs women regarding hand placement at takbir and state the exceptional cases.

Core Idea
Men remove hands from sleeves at takbir; women keep them in sleeves for modesty unless cold.

The third adab concerns the opening takbir. Men are to expose their hands as a sign of humility, while women keep them covered. There is also a warning about moving hands carelessly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Removing palms from sleeves at the first takbir.
2
Understand the wisdom
Closer to humility, distant from arrogance, allows finger spreading.
3
Note gender difference
Men remove hands; women keep them in sleeves for modesty.
4
Consider exceptions
Necessity (cold) allows women to keep hands in sleeves; general rule is as much as possible.
5
Be aware of invalidation risk
If without excuse sounds (letters) are produced, it can invalidate prayer.

Etiquettes of Prayer: Cough, Standing, and Imam's Start
Explains three etiquettes: cough suppression, standing at 'Hayya ala al-falah', and imam starting at 'Qad qamat al-salah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three etiquettes of prayer regarding cough suppression, timing of standing, and imam's commencement, and explain the Hanafi flexibility in timing for standing and takbir.

Core Idea
In Hanafi salah, the timing for standing and imam's start is flexible; delaying until iqamah ends is permissible by consensus.

Prayer has many etiquettes that enhance its perfection. Among them are suppressing a cough, standing at the right moment during iqamah, and the imam beginning at the appropriate time. This lesson clarifies these three etiquettes and highlights the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify each etiquette and its ruling level
The text mentions three: suppressing cough, standing, and imam's start. They are classified as adab (sunnah muakkadah), not fard or wajib.
The ruling level for each is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Examine the timing of standing
The passage gives conditions: if the imam is near the mihrab, stand at 'Hayya ala al-falah'; if far, each row stands when the imam reaches them. Zufar holds a different view about the exact moment.
Zufar says stand at the first 'Qad qamat al-salah'.
3
Understand the imam's start
The imam may begin the prayer at 'Qad qamat al-salah' or delay until the iqamah is complete. Abu Yusuf's view that delaying is fine is supported by consensus.
Delaying is explicitly permitted.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Zufar's view differs from the majority on both standing and imam's start. The mufta bihi is the flexible position.
Ikhtilaf within the school is legitimate.
5
Apply the flexibility
In practice, one may choose an earlier or later timing; the prayer remains valid either way.
Consensus confirms no harm in delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودفع السعال ما استطاع، والقيام حين قيل: "حي على الفلاح"، وشروع الإمام مذ قيل: قد قامت الصلاة. شرح: القيام حين قيل إلخ: أي حين يقول المؤذن في الإقامة مسارعة لامتثال الأمر، هذا إذا كان الإمام بقرب المحراب، فإن لم يكن وقف كل صف ينتهي إليه الإمام على الأصح، ولو دخل من أمامهم قاموا حين يقع بصرهم عليه، وقال زفر حين قيل قد قامت الصلاة الأولى، ويحرمون عند الثانية. (فتح) الصلاة: في المرة الأولى، ولو أخر حتى أتمها لا بأس به إجماعاً، وهو قول أبي يوسف.
And suppressing cough as much as possible, and standing when it is said 'Hayya ala al-falah', and the imam's beginning from when it is said 'Qad qamat al-salah'. Explanation: 'standing when it is said etc.' i.e. when the muadhdhin says it in the iqamah, hastening to obey the command. This is if the imam is near the mihrab; if not, each row stops where the imam reaches, according to the most correct view. If one enters from ahead of them, they stand when their sight falls on him. Zufar said: when it is said 'Qad qamat al-salah' the first time, and they say the takbir to commence at the second time. (Fath) 'al-salah' in the first time, and if one delays until completing it, there is no harm by consensus, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage covers the fourth, fifth, and sixth etiquettes of prayer. The fourth is suppressing a cough as much as possible, because it is not part of the actions of prayer and could produce speech that invalidates. The fifth is to stand when the muadhdhin says 'Hayya ala al-falah' during iqamah, as an act of compliance. The exact timing depends on the imam's proximity. If the imam is near, they stand at 'Hayya ala al-falah'; if not, each row stands when the imam reaches their row. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) holds that they stand at the first 'Qad qamat al-salah' and commence (say takbir) at the second. The relied-upon view is to stand at the first 'Qad qamat' or even later; it is permissible to delay standing until the iqamah is complete, by consensus. The sixth etiquette is that the imam should start the prayer when the muadhdhin says 'Qad qamat al-salah' the first time (according to some) or wait until the end; the passage indicates that it is acceptable to start after the iqamah is finished, which is the view of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
دفع السعال (dafʿ al-suʿāl): Suppressing a cough during prayer as much as possible.
حي على الفلاح (ḥayya ʿalā al-falāḥ): A phrase in iqamah calling to success; when heard, congregation stands.
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qāmat al-ṣalāh): The final phrase of iqamah indicating prayer is about to begin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on suppressing a cough during prayer?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is haram to cough.
C) It is sunnah to suppress as much as possible.
D) It is mandatory to cough to clear throat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides flexibility in the etiquettes of prayer; delaying standing or imam's start until iqamah ends is permissible by consensus.

The Six Adab (Etiquettes) of Prayer
Lists and explains six recommended acts of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six etiquettes of prayer, state their hukm level, and explain the Hanafi proof for suppressing a yawn.

Core Idea
The six adab are recommended, not obligatory—they perfect the prayer but do not invalidate it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the six internal etiquettes of prayer, which the Hanafi school classifies as adab (recommended acts) rather than sunnah or wajib. Understanding these helps you refine your prayer without worry of invalidation. We will examine each adab, the proof for the second, and the intra-Hanafi differences regarding when to stand for iqamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of six acts
Read the passage and extract the six etiquettes: looking at prostration spot, suppressing yawn, taking hands out, repelling cough, standing at 'Hayya al-falah', and Imam starting at 'Qad qamat al-salah'.
These are internal acts of prayer, distinct from external conditions.
2
Determine the hukm level of each
The text labels them as 'adab', which in the Hanafi school are recommended (sunnah ghayr muakkadah). They are not fard or wajib; omitting them does not affect validity.
Adab are lower than sunnah muakkadah; they complete the prayer but are not required.
3
Locate the dalil for suppressing the yawn
The passage quotes a hadith: 'When one of you yawns, let him suppress it with his hand...' This is ahad hadith, hence zanni in transmission, but its meaning is clear.
The command 'fliridduhu' indicates recommendation, not obligation, per Hanafi usul.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof's operative phrase is the imperative 'fliridduhu'. In Hanafi usul, an imperative without qarinah indicates wujub, but here the context (yawning is from shaytan) and the phrase 'ma istata'a' (as much as possible) indicate it is a recommendation, not an obligation.
The presence of 'ma istata'a' tempers the command to a recommendation.
5
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For the fifth adab (standing at 'Hayya al-falah'), Zufar held that they stand at the first 'Qad qamat al-salah', while the relied-upon view is at the second. For the sixth, Abu Yusuf permits delaying the Imam's start until the iqamah is completed.
These differences do not affect the overall hukm level; they are about optimal timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و آدابها: نظره إلى موضع سجوده وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب، وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير، ودفع السعال ما استطاع، والقيام حين قيل: "حي على الفلاح"، وشروع الإمام مذ قيل: قد قامت الصلاة. و آدابها: أي آداب الصلاة ستة على ما ذكره، الأوّل: نظره أي نظر المصلي. سجوده: قائماً وإلى قدميه راكعاً، وإلى حجره قاعداً، وإلى أرنبة أنفه ساجداً، وإلى منكبه الأيمن والأيسر حالة التسليمتين. (ط) وكظم فمه: [ أي إمساكه ولو يأخذ شفة بأسنانه] خوفاً من ضحك الشيطان منه بفعله؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده بيده ما استطاع، فإن أحدكم إذا تثاءب ضحك منه الشيطان"، وكأنه فيه من التكاسل فيما محله النشاط والخضوع والتثاؤب مهموز كما في المصباح. (فتح) التثاؤب: لأنه من الشيطان وإن تعذر يضع ظهر الكف على الفم. وإخراج كفيه: لأنه أقرب للتواضع، وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة، وأمكن من نشر الأصابع، وهذا في حق الرجال، وأما في حق النساء فجعل يديها في كميها؛ لأنه أسترلها. (فتح) عند التكبير: أي عند التكبير الأول إلا لضرورة كبرد وأما المرأة فتجعل في كميها ما استطاع: يعني مهما أمكن؛ لأنه ليس من أفعال الصلاة، ولو كان بلا عذر فحصلت منه حروف تفسد صلاته. (ع) حين قيل إلخ [ أي حين يقول المؤذن في الإقامة. (ط)] مسارعة لامتثال الأمر، هذا إذا كان الإمام بقرب المحراب، فإن لم يكن وقف كل صف ينتهي إليه الإمام على الأصح، ولو دخل من أمامهم قاموا حين يقع بصرهم عليه، وقال زفر حين قيل قد قامت الصلاة الأولى، ويحرمون عند الثانية. (فتح) الصلاة: في المرة الأولى، ولو أخر حتى أتمها لا بأس به إجماعاً، وهو قول أبي يوسف.
And its etiquettes: his looking to the place of his prostration, and suppressing his mouth at the time of yawning, and taking out his palms from his sleeves at the time of takbir, and repelling coughing as much as possible, and standing when it is said: 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', and the Imam's starting when it is said: 'Qad qamat al-salah'. And its etiquettes: that is, the etiquettes of prayer are six, as he mentioned. First: his looking, i.e., the looking of the worshipper: to his prostration when standing, to his feet when bowing, to his lap when sitting, to the tip of his nose when prostrating, and to his right and left shoulder at the time of the two salutations. (t) And suppressing his mouth: [i.e., holding it, even by taking his lip with his teeth] out of fear of the devil laughing at him due to his action; because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you yawns, let him suppress it with his hand as much as possible, for when one of you yawns, the devil laughs at him.' And it seems that there is in it laziness in what is a place of activity and humility, and yawning is with hamzah as in al-Misbah. (Fath) Yawning: because it is from the devil, and if difficult, he places the back of his hand on his mouth. And taking out his hands: because it is closer to humility, farther from resembling the arrogant, and more enabling for spreading the fingers. This applies to men; as for women, they place their hands inside their sleeves because it is more covering for them. (Fath) At the time of takbir: i.e., at the first takbir except for necessity such as cold. As for the woman, she places them in her sleeves as much as possible: meaning as much as she is able; because it is not from the actions of prayer, and if it is without excuse and letters result from it, it invalidates his prayer. (Ayn) When it is said etc. [i.e., when the muadhdhin says it in the iqamah. (t)] Hastening to comply with the command. This is if the Imam is near the mihrab. If not, each row stands at its end reaching the Imam according to the most correct view. If someone enters in front of them, they stand when their sight falls on him. Zufar said: when it is said 'Qad qamat al-salah' the first time, and they pronounce the tahrimah at the second time. (Fath) The salah: in the first time, and if he delays until he completes it, there is no harm by consensus, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage lists and explains the six internal etiquettes (adab) of prayer as found in the Hanafi school. The first etiquette is looking at the place of prostration while standing, at the feet while bowing, at the lap while sitting, at the tip of the nose while prostrating, and at the right and left shoulder during the two salutations. The second is suppressing the mouth when yawning, supported by a hadith that yawning is from Satan and one should try to hold it back; if difficult, one may place the back of the hand on the mouth. The third is taking the hands out of the sleeves during the first takbir for men, as it shows humility; women keep their hands inside their sleeves for modesty. The fourth is repelling coughing as much as possible, and if it produces intelligible letters without excuse, it invalidates the prayer. The fifth is standing when the muadhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' in the iqamah, provided the Imam is near the mihrab; otherwise, rows stand as they reach the Imam. Zufar held that they stand at the first 'Qad qamat al-salah' and pronounce the tahrimah at the second, but the preferred view is the first. The sixth is that the Imam begins when 'Qad qamat al-salah' is said the first time, though delaying until completion is permissible by consensus, as stated by Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
آداب الصلاة (adab al-salah): The six recommended etiquettes of prayer that enhance its perfection; not obligatory.
كظم الفم (kazm al-fam): Suppressing the mouth during a yawn, either by using the hand or taking the lip with the teeth.
التسليمتين (al-taslimatayn): The two salutations (saying Salam to the right and left) at the end of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six etiquettes of prayer mentioned in the passage?
A) Looking at the place of prostration
B) Suppressing the mouth when yawning
C) Raising hands to the ears at takbir
D) Standing when 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' is said

Key Takeaway
The six adab of prayer are recommended but not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer, but adhering to them perfects one's devotion.

The Follower's Takbir: Concurrence or Connection?
Explains the rulings on the follower's takbir and the internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's takbir during congregational prayer and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa from those of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
The follower's takbir must align with the imam's; the virtue of tahrimah is only attained by concurrence according to Abu Hanifa.

In congregational prayer, the follower's takbir is not independent; it is tied to the imam's. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether the follower should strictly synchronize his takbir with the imam's or whether he can lag slightly. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the basis for the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the follower saying the opening takbir (tahrimah). The ruling is that it must be said, but the timing relative to the imam is disputed.
The takbir itself is fard; the timing is about achieving the optimal virtue.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says the follower should make his takbir coincide exactly (محاذاة) with the imam's takbir. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say he should connect (اتصال) his takbir, i.e., start immediately after the imam finishes.
The phrase 'وعندهما: يوصله بتكبيره' indicates the Sahibayn's view.
3
Understand the consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, the virtue of the tahrimah is only attained by concurrence. According to the two, it is attained until the completion of the thana' (the opening praise).
This has practical implications for when the follower's prayer is considered valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية الصلاة فصل: [ أي في كيفية تركيب أفعال الصلاة] هو لغة: الحاجز، وعرفاً طائفة من المسائل داخلة تحت كتاب، وهو مصدر يحتمل أن يكون بمعنى الفاعل كرجل عدل أي فاصل بين ما ذكر قبله ، وبعده، ويحتمل أن يكون بمعنى المفعول، والمعنى هذا مفصول عما قبله فإن ذكرت بعده "في" يرفع وينون على أنه مبتدأ محذوف أي هذا فصل، وإن لم تذكر بعده "في" سكن آخره؛ لأنك إذا وقفت على كلمة سكنت آخرها، والأحكام المذكورة في هذا الفصل مشتركة بين المصلين والمختص بالمقتدي أن يحاذي تكبيره تكبير إمامه وأنه أفضل عنده، وعندهما: يوصله بتكبيره أي يوصل ألف "الله" براء "أكبر"، ولا تدرك فضيلة التحريمة عنده إلا بالمحاذاة، وعندهما إلى الفراغ الثناء في الأصح. (فتح) كبر أي قال: الله أكبر، وإذا حذف المصلي أو الحالف أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة أو حذف الهاء اختلف في صحة تحريمته وانعقاد يمينه وحل ذبيحته، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً. (فتح) إلا إذا كان أخرس أو أمياً لا يحسن شيئاً فدخولهما بالنية فقط، ولا يلزمهما تحريك اللسان. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٦/١] ورفع يديه: [مقدما على التكبير وعند أبي يوسف مقارنا معه، قوله: "حذاء أذنيه" والأمة كالرجل، والحرة ترفع حذاء منكبيها، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد في حق الرجل عيني طائي وكيفيته أن يرفع يديه حتى يحاذي بإلهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، وبرؤوس الأصابع فروع أذنيه، وقال الشافعي حذاء منكبيه؛ لأنه وأصحابه كانوا يرفعون إلى المناكب، ولنا حديث وائل بن حجر أنه علي كان إذا كبر يرفع يديه حذاء أذنيه، وما رواه محمول على حالة العذر؛ لأن وائلاً قال: ثم أتيت من العام المقبل وعليهم الأكسية والبرانس، فكانوا يرفعون فيها إلى مناكبهم، فعلم أن ذلك كان لعذر البرد. (فتح)
Chapter on the manner of prayer. Fasl: [i.e., on the composition of the actions of prayer] It is linguistically: a barrier, and conventionally: a group of issues under a book. It is a verbal noun that can mean the doer, like a just man, i.e., a separator between what came before and after, or the object, meaning this is separated from what preceded. If 'fi' follows it, it is raised and nunated as a deleted mubtada, i.e., 'this is a chapter'. If 'fi' does not follow, it is made silent at the end. The rulings mentioned in this chapter are common to all worshippers, but specific to the follower is that his takbir should coincide with his imam's takbir, and that it is better according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he connects his takbir, i.e., connects the alif of 'Allah' with the ra' of 'Akbar'. The virtue of tahrimah is only attained by concurrence according to him, while according to them it is attained until the completion of the praise according to the most correct view. (Fath) 'He said takbir' means he said 'Allahu Akbar'. If the worshipper, or the one swearing an oath, or the one slaughtering omits the madd on the second lam of the Majestic Name or omits the ha', there is a difference of opinion on the validity of his tahrimah, his oath, and the lawfulness of his slaughter. So one should not do that as a precaution. (Fath) Except if he is mute or illiterate knowing nothing, then they enter (the prayer) by intention only, and moving the tongue is not required of them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq) And raising his hands: [Before the takbir according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf simultaneous with it. His saying: 'opposite his ears' applies to the slave woman like the man, while the free woman raises opposite her shoulders. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad held this view for the man. (Ayn Tayy?) The manner is that he raises his hands until his thumbs are opposite the lobes of his ears and his fingertips are opposite the tops of his ears. Al-Shafi'i said: opposite his shoulders, because he and his companions used to raise to the shoulders. Our proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he said takbir, raised his hands opposite his ears. What he (Wa'il) narrated is interpreted as a case of excuse, because Wa'il said: 'Then I came the following year and they were wearing cloaks and hooded garments, so they raised to their shoulders.' Thus it is known that was due to the cold. (Fath)
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter heading 'Fasl fi Kayfiyyat al-Salah' and begins by defining 'fasl' linguistically and terminologically. It then explains that the rulings in this chapter cover both the imam and the follower. Specifically, for the follower, Abu Hanifa holds that it is better for his takbir to coincide exactly with the imam's takbir, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that he should connect his takbir, meaning he begins immediately after the imam finishes. The virtue of the tahrimah (the opening takbir) is only attained by concurrence according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two, it is attained until the completion of the thana' (praise). The passage then discusses the proper pronunciation of the takbir: it must be 'Allahu Akbar'. Omitting the madd on the second lam of 'Allah' or omitting the ha' is problematic and should be avoided. For a mute or illiterate person, mere intention suffices without moving the tongue. Regarding raising the hands, Abu Hanifa holds that hands are raised before the takbir, while Abu Yusuf says simultaneously. The height for men is to the earlobes, for a slave woman likewise, but a free woman raises to her shoulders. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr that the Prophet raised his hands to his ears, and the report from al-Shafi'i that they raised to shoulders is explained by the cold weather causing them to wear heavy garments.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer valid and prohibits worldly talk.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer.
المحاذاة (al-muhadhat): Exact concurrence or alignment of the follower's takbir with the imam's.
الاتصال (al-ittisal): Connection, i.e., the follower says his takbir immediately after the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) regarding the follower's takbir timing?
A) It must exactly coincide with the imam's takbir.
B) It must be said immediately after the imam's takbir (connection).
C) The follower may say his takbir at any time.
D) The follower should not say takbir; he just intends.

Key Takeaway
The follower's takbir must be connected to the imam's; the most practiced view is that it can be slightly after, but the virtue of tahrimah is attained by concurrence per Abu Hanifa.

Raising Hands in Prayer: Height and Timing
Explains the hand raising practice and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the height and timing of raising hands during the opening takbir and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Hanafis raise hands to the ears; Shafi'is to the shoulders. The Hanafi proof from Wa'il ibn Hujr prevails.

One of the most visible differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is the height at which hands are raised during the opening takbir. This lesson examines the evidence, the Hanafi response to the opposing proof, and the related timing dispute within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Men raise their hands so that thumbs are opposite earlobes and fingertips opposite tops of ears. Free women raise to shoulders.
This is a sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Ahmad raise hands to shoulders for men.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr reporting that the Prophet raised his hands to his ears.
This is a dalil naqli.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof (also from Wa'il but raising to shoulders) is explained by an excuse: cold weather causing them to wear cloaks, so they raised only to shoulders.
Thus the original practice is to the ears.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi timing dispute
Abu Hanifa raises hands before the takbir; Abu Yusuf simultaneously.
The mufta bihi is before the takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
